   AGENCY: The Illinois environmental protection agency.
   BOARD: The Illinois pollution control board.
   MAXIMUM SETBACK ZONE: The area around a community water supply well
established under section 14.3 of the act and this section, and described in
appendix A attached to the ordinance codified herein.
   MINIMUM SETBACK ZONE: The area around a community water supply well
established under section 14.2 of the act and this section, and described in
appendix A attached to the ordinance codified herein.
   C.   Prohibitions: With respect to well no. 4 (IEPA #52049), well no. 3
(IEPA #52048) and well no. 5 (IEPA #01527):
      1.   Except as provided in subsection D or E of this section, no person
shall place a new potential primary source, new potential secondary source, or
new potential route within the minimum setback zone.
      2.   Except as provided in subsection D of this section, no person shall
place a new potential primary source within the maximum setback zone unless the
source is placed beyond one thousand feet (1,000') from the wellhead.
      3.   Except as provided in subsection D of this section, no person shall
place a new potential primary route within the maximum setback zone.
   D.   Waivers, Exceptions And Certifications Of Minimal Hazard:
      1.   If, pursuant to section 14.2(b) of the act, the owner of a new
potential primary source, new potential secondary source, or new potential
route is granted a waiver by the agency, such owner shall be deemed to have a
waiver to the same extent from subsection C1 of this section.
      2.   If, pursuant to section 14.2(c) of the act, the owner of a new
potential primary source (other than land filling or land treating), new
potential secondary source, or new potential route is granted an exception by
the board, such owner shall be deemed to have an exception to the same extent
from subsection C1 of this section.
      3.   If, pursuant to section 14.2(c) of the act, the owner of a new
potential primary source (other than land filling or land treating) is granted
an exception by the board, such owner shall be deemed to have an exception to
the same extent from subsection C2 of this section.
      4.   If, pursuant to section 14.5 of the act, the owner of a new
potential primary source, new potential secondary source, or new potential
route is issued a certificate of minimal hazard by the agency, such owner shall
not be subject to subsection C1 of this section to the same extent that such
owner is not subject to section 14.2(d) of the act.
   E.   Exclusion: Subsection C1 of this section shall not apply to new common
sources of sanitary pollution as specified pursuant to section 17 of the act
and the regulations adopted thereunder by the agency; however, no such common
sources may be located within the applicable minimum distance from a community
water supply well specified by such regulations. (Ord. 11-2005, 5-9-2005)
 
Notes
1 1. 415 ILCS 55/1 et seq.
2 2. 415 ILCS 5/1 et seq.
3-6-2: USE OF GROUNDWATER AS POTABLE WATER PROHIBITED:
   A.   Definitions: As used in this section, the following words and terms
shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this subsection:
    PERSON: Any individual, partnership, copartnership, firm, company, limited
liability company, corporation, association, joint stock company, trust,
estate, political subdivision, or any other legal entity, or their legal
representatives, agents or assigns.
   POTABLE WATER: Any water used for human or domestic consumption including,
but not limited to, water used for drinking, bathing, swimming, washing dishes
or preparing foods.
   B.   Areas Where Use Prohibited: The use of, or attempted use of,
groundwater from within the corporate limits of the city as a potable water
supply by the installation or drilling of wells or by any other method is
hereby prohibited. This prohibition expressly includes the city. (Ord. 18-2005,
10-10-2005)
   C.   Penalty: Any person violating the provisions of this section shall be
subject to a fine of up to seven hundred fifty dollars ($750.00) for each
violation. (Ord. 18-2005, 10-10-2005; amd. 2017 Code)
CHAPTER 7
ABANDONED, INOPERABLE VEHICLES
SECTION:
3-7-1: Definitions
3-7-2: Inoperable Vehicles
3-7-3: Abandonment Of Vehicles Prohibited
3-7-4: Notice Of Possible Towing; Hearing
3-7-5: Notice To Police Of Abandoned, Lost Or Other Vehicle
3-7-6: Authority To Tow; Responsibility For Costs
3-7-7: Reclamation Of Towed Vehicle
3-7-8: Newer Vehicles
3-7-9: Older Vehicles
3-7-10: Recordkeeping
3-7-11: Disposition Of Revenues
3-7-12: Nonliability Of City Or Towing Service
3-7-13: Penalty
3-7-1: DEFINITIONS:
For the purpose of this chapter, the following words and terms shall have the
meanings ascribed to them in this section:
ABANDONED VEHICLE: Any motor vehicle or other vehicle in a state of disrepair
rendering the vehicle incapable of being driven in its condition.
HIGHWAY: Any street, alley, or public way within the city of Athens.
INOPERABLE VEHICLE: Any motor vehicle or other vehicle incapable of or
prohibited from being driven on any highway due to disrepair or disuse. Any
vehicle not displaying valid registration plates or proper evidence of
application therefor will be presumed to be inoperable for purposes of this
chapter. (Ord. 03-99, 4-12-1999; amd. Ord. 06-2014, 7-14-2014)
3-7-2: INOPERABLE VEHICLES:
   A.   No person shall leave any inoperable vehicle, or parts thereof, for
fourteen (14) consecutive days or more in any area, public or private, in view
of the public or outside any building. Any person in violation of this
subsection shall be fined not less than seventy five dollars ($75.00) nor more
than five hundred dollars ($500.00) for each violation. Each day such violation
is committed or permitted to continue shall constitute a separate offense and
shall be punishable hereunder as such. (Ord. 03-99, 4-12-1999; amd. 2017 Code)
   B.   An inoperable vehicle which has no readily ascertainable owner or
bailee will be presumed an "abandoned vehicle", as defined in section
3-7-1 of this chapter, for the purposes of this chapter. (Ord. 03-99, 4-12-
1999)
3-7-3: ABANDONMENT OF VEHICLES PROHIBITED:
   A.   Highways: The abandonment of a motor vehicle or other vehicle or any
part thereof on any highway in the city is unlawful and subject to penalties as
set forth herein.
   B.   Property Other Than Highways:
      1.   The abandonment of a motor vehicle or other vehicle, or any part
thereof, on private or public property, other than a highway, in view of the
general public, anywhere in the city is unlawful except on the property of the
owner or bailee of such abandoned vehicle. (Ord. 03-99, 4-12-1999)
      2.   A motor vehicle or other vehicle, not properly licensed or
registered, or any part thereof, so abandoned on private property may be
authorized for removal by or upon the order of the chief of police. If such
vehicle is properly licensed and registered, then such vehicle cannot be towed
until notice and an opportunity for hearing can be accorded to the owner
pursuant to section
3-7-4 of this chapter. (Ord. 03-99, 4-12-1999; amd. 2017 Code)
3-7-4: NOTICE OF POSSIBLE TOWING; HEARING:
If a motor vehicle or other vehicle is properly registered and displays current
registration plates and is subject to any provision of this chapter under which
towing of such vehicle may be authorized, then notice and opportunity for
hearing on the matter must be accorded to the registered owner before towing.
The mayor shall preside at such hearing and he/she shall decide whether the
applicable city department has authority to tow the vehicle in question
pursuant to the provisions of this chapter. The notice of hearing shall be in
substantially the following form: (Ord. 03-99, 4-12-1999)
   NOTICE
NAME                                       
ADDRESS                                    
A vehicle described as:
Make                      
Year                      
Color                     
with registration plates #             is registered in your name with the
Secretary of State of Illinois. This vehicle has been located at (location) and
is in violation of title 3, chapter 7 of the Athens City Code, "Abandoned,
Inoperable Vehicles". This violation subjects your vehicle to towing and if you
are found guilty of the offense described thereunder, you are subject to a
fine. In addition, the costs of towing will be assessed against you.
If you wish to have a hearing on the matter of towing, you must notify the
Police within five (5) days of receipt of this notice. At that time, a hearing
date will be set. If you do not wish to have a hearing or fail to notify the
Police within five (5) days of receipt of this notice, then your vehicle is
subject to immediate towing.
(Ord. 03-99, 4-12-1999; amd. 2017 Code)
3-7-5: NOTICE TO POLICE OF ABANDONED, LOST OR OTHER VEHICLE:
   A.   When an abandoned, lost, stolen or unclaimed motor vehicle or other
vehicle comes into the temporary possession or custody of a person in the city,
not the owner of the vehicle, such person shall immediately notify the chief of
police. (Ord. 03-99, 4-12-1999; amd. 2017 Code)
   B.   Upon receipt of such notification, the chief of police shall authorize
a towing service to remove and take possession of the abandoned, lost, stolen
or unclaimed motor vehicle or other vehicle. The towing service will safely
keep the towed vehicle and its contents, maintain a record of the tow until the
vehicle is claimed by the owner or any other person legally entitled to
possession thereof, or until it is disposed of as provided in this chapter.
(Ord. 03-99, 4-12-1999)
3-7-6: AUTHORITY TO TOW; RESPONSIBILITY FOR COSTS:
   A.   When a motor vehicle or other vehicle is abandoned on a highway in the
city ten (10) hours or more, its removal by a towing service may be authorized
by order of the chief of police.
   B.   When an abandoned, unattended, wrecked, burned or partially dismantled
motor vehicle or other vehicle is creating a traffic hazard because of its
position in relation to the highway or its physical appearance is causing the
impeding of traffic, its immediate removal by a towing service may be
authorized by order of the chief of police.
   C.   When a vehicle's removal from either public or private property is
authorized by order of the chief of police, the owner of the vehicle will be
responsible for all towing charges unless acquitted of the offense charged
under this chapter. (Ord. 03-99, 4-12-1999)
3-7-7: RECLAMATION OF TOWED VEHICLE:
Any time before a motor vehicle or other vehicle is sold at public sale or
disposed of as provided herein, the owner, lienholder or other person legally
entitled to its possession may reclaim the vehicle by presenting to the chief
of police proof of ownership or proof of the right to possession of the
vehicle. No vehicle shall be released to the owner, lienholder or other person
under this section until all towing, storage and processing charges have been
paid. (Ord. 03-99, 4-12-1999; amd. 2017 Code)
3-7-8: NEWER VEHICLES:
   A.   Whenever an abandoned, lost, stolen or unclaimed motor vehicle or other
vehicle seven (7) years of age or newer remains unclaimed by the registered
owner, lienholder or other person legally entitled to its possession for a
period of thirty (30) days after notice has been given as provided herein, the
police department shall cause it to be sold at public sale to a person licensed
as an automotive parts recycler, rebuilder or scrap processor or the towing
operator which towed the vehicle.
   B.   Notice of the time and place of the sale shall be posted in a
conspicuous place for at least ten (10) days prior to the sale on the premises
where the vehicle has been impounded. At least ten (10) days prior to the sale,
the police department shall cause a notice of the time and place of the sale to
be sent by certified mail to the registered owner, lienholder or other person
known by the police department or towing service to be legally entitled to the
possession of the vehicle. Such notice shall contain a complete description of
the vehicle to be sold and what steps must be taken by any legally entitled
person to reclaim the vehicle. (Ord. 03-99, 4-12-1999; amd. 2017 Code)
   C.   In those instances where the certified notification specified herein
has been returned by the postal authorities to the police department due to the
addressee having moved or being unknown at the address obtained from the
registration records of this state, the sending of a second certified notice
will not be required. (Ord. 03-99, 4-12-1999)
   D.   When the identity of the owner, lienholder or other person legally
entitled to the possession of an abandoned, lost or unclaimed vehicle of seven
(7) years of age or newer cannot be determined by any means provided in this
chapter, the vehicle may be sold as provided in this chapter or disposed of in
the manner authorized herein without notice to any person whose identity cannot
be determined. (Ord. 03-99, 4-12-1999; amd. 2017 Code)
3-7-9: OLDER VEHICLES:
When an abandoned vehicle of more than seven (7) years of age is impounded as
specified by this chapter, it will be kept in custody for a minimum of ten (10)
days for the purpose of determining the ownership and contacting the owner by
the U.S. mail, public service or in person for a determination of disposition.
At the expiration of the ten (10) day period, without the benefit of
disposition information being received from the owner, the police department
may authorize the disposition of said vehicle as in subsection 3-7-8D of this
chapter for the disposal of the vehicle as junk only. (Ord. 03-99, 4-12-1999;
amd. Ord. 17-2003, 11-10-2003)
3-7-10: RECORDKEEPING:
   A.   Towed Vehicles: When a motor vehicle or other vehicle is authorized to
be towed, the police department shall keep and maintain a record of the vehicle
towed, listing the color, year of manufacture, manufacturer's trade name,
manufacturer's series name, body style, vehicle identification number, and
license plate year and number displayed on the vehicle. The record shall also
include the date and hour of tow, location towed from, location towed to,
reason for towing, and the name of the officer authorizing the tow. (Ord. 03-
99, 4-12-1999)
   B.   Reclaimed Or Sold Vehicles: When a motor vehicle or other vehicle in
the custody of the police department is reclaimed by the registered owner,
lienholder or other legally entitled person, or when the vehicle is sold at
public sale or otherwise disposed of as provided in this chapter, a report of
the transaction will be maintained by the police department for a period of one
year from the date of sale or disposal. (Ord. 03-99, 4-12-1999; amd. 2017 Code)
3-7-11: DISPOSITION OF REVENUES:
When a vehicle located within the corporate limits of the city is authorized to
be towed by the police department and disposed of as set forth in this chapter,
the proceeds of the public sale or disposition after the deduction of towing,
storage and processing charges shall be deposited in the municipal treasury.
(Ord. 03-99, 4-12-1999; amd. 2017 Code)
3-7-12: NONLIABILITY OF CITY OR TOWING SERVICE:
No authorized city employee or towing service owner, operator or employee shall
be held to answer or be liable for damages in any action brought by the
registered owner, former registered owner, or his legal representative,
lienholder or any other person legally entitled to the possession of a motor
vehicle or other vehicle when the vehicle was processed and sold or disposed of
as provided by this chapter. (Ord. 03-99, 4-12-1999; amd. 2017 Code)
3-7-13: PENALTY:
Any person convicted of violating any provision of this chapter, except
subsection 3-7-2A of this chapter, shall be fined in an amount not less than
two hundred dollars ($200.00) nor more than seven hundred fifty dollars
($750.00). Each day such violation is committed or permitted to continue shall
constitute a separate offense and shall be punishable hereunder as such. (Ord.
03-99, 4-12-1999; amd. 2017 Code)
TITLE 4
POLICE AND PUBLIC SAFETY
CHAPTER 1
POLICE OFFICERS
SECTION:
4-1-1: Part Time Police
4-1-2: Auxiliary Police
4-1-1: PART TIME POLICE:
   A.   Training: All police officers, other than those officers who shall be
employed on a full time basis, shall be required to be qualified and
successfully complete any training mandated by the Illinois law enforcement
training and standards board.
   B.   Hiring Standards: Part time police officers may be hired by the city,
as authorized by statute, in accordance with the following hiring standards:
      1.   The applicant must be a U.S. citizen;
      2.   The applicant must be twenty one (21) years of age or older;
      3.   The applicant must possess a high school diploma or GED equivalency;
      4.   The applicant must have a valid driver's license;
      5.   The applicant must have no felony convictions; and
      6.   The applicant must meet all standards set forth in 430 Illinois
Compiled Statutes 65/0.01 et seq., pertaining to the firearms owners
identification act.
   C.   Responsibilities: A part time police officer shall have all the
responsibilities of a full time police officer, but the number of hours a part
time officer may work within a calendar year is restricted.
   D.   Submission Of Provisions To State: The aforesaid hiring standards,
particularly with respect to part time police officers employed by the city,
shall be submitted to the Illinois law enforcement training and standards
board, as required by statute. (Ord. 12-2012, 8-13-2012)
4-1-2: AUXILIARY POLICE:
   A.   Appointment: The mayor may, with the advice and consent of the city
council, appoint auxiliary police officers, not to exceed eight (8) in number,
from names furnished the mayor by the chief of police. (Ord. 10-2007, 9-10-
2007)
   B.   Conservators Of The Peace: Auxiliary police officers shall not be
members of the regular police department and shall possess conservator of the
peace powers as defined in section 3.1-15-25 of the Illinois municipal code 1 .
(Ord. 10-2007, 9-10-2007; amd. 2017 Code)
   C.   Powers And Duties: Auxiliary police officers shall serve at the
direction and control of the chief of police and shall have the following
powers and duties:
      1.   To aid or direct traffic in the city.
      2.   To aid in the control of natural or manmade disasters.
      3.   To aid in case of civil disorder.
      4.   To act at the direction and control of the chief of police in any
other activity, other than those activities traditionally reserved to those who
are vested with conservator of the peace powers.
   D.   Uniforms And Identification: Auxiliary police officers may wear
uniforms. Uniforms and identification symbols worn by auxiliary police officers
must be different and distinct from those worn by regular police officers.
   E.   Firearms:
      1.   Auxiliary police officers may, with prior permission of the chief of
police, carry firearms while on duty.
      2.   All auxiliary police officers shall successfully complete the forty
(40) hour mandatory firearms training course before being permitted to carry a
firearm, as specified in section 3.1-30-20 of the Illinois municipal code 2 .
Upon completion of the course of training, the chief of police shall file a
certificate attesting to the auxiliary police officer's successful completion
of the required forty (40) hour mandatory firearms training course.
   F.   Compensation: Auxiliary police officers shall receive no compensation
for services rendered. (Ord. 10-2007, 9-10-2007)
 
Notes
1 1. 65 ILCS 5/3.11-15-25.
2 2. 65 ILCS 5/3.1-30-20.
CHAPTER 2
ANIMAL CONTROL
ARTICLE A.  DOGS
SECTION:
4-2A-1: Definitions
4-2A-2: Rabies Inoculation Requirements
4-2A-3: Number Of Dogs Restricted
4-2A-4: Restraint Of Dogs
4-2A-5: Nuisance Dogs
4-2A-6: Impoundment And Redemption Provisions
4-2A-7: Enforcement Official
4-2A-8: Penalties
4-2A-1: DEFINITIONS:
AT LARGE: Off the premises of the owner or custodian of the dog and not under
the immediate control of the owner or custodian.
COUNTY BOARD: The county board of Menard County, Illinois.
DEPARTMENT OF AGRICULTURE: The department of agriculture of the state of
Illinois.
DOG: All members of the family Canidae.
INOCULATION AGAINST RABIES: The injection of an antirabies vaccine approved by
the department of agriculture.
LEASH: A cord, rope, strap or chain which shall be securely fastened to a
collar or harness of a dog and shall be of sufficient strength to keep such dog
under control.
OWNER: Any person having a right of property in a dog, or who keeps or harbors
a dog, or who knowingly permits a dog to remain on or about any premises
occupied by him or her.
POUND: Any facility approved by the county board or the mayor and city council
for the purpose of enforcing the animal control act of the state of Illinois
and used as a shelter for seized, stray, homeless, abandoned, or unchained
dogs.
RESTRAINT: A dog is under restraint within the meaning of this article if he is
controlled by a leash; at heel beside a responsible person, or obedient to that
person's commands; within a vehicle being driven or parked on the streets; or
within the property limits of his owner or custodian. (Ord. 04-98, 5-11-1998;
amd. Ord. 01-2007, 3-12-2007)
4-2A-2: RABIES INOCULATION REQUIREMENTS:
   A.   Inoculation And Tag Required: Each calendar year, or at such intervals
as may hereafter be promulgated by the department of agriculture, every owner
or custodian of a dog four (4) months or more of age shall cause such dog to be
inoculated against rabies. Such owner or custodian of such dog shall cause a
serially numbered tag evidencing such inoculation to be attached to a collar or
harness worn by the dog.
   B.   Veterinarian To Inoculate And Provide Certificate And Tag: The
inoculation of dogs required by subsection A of this section shall be performed
by a veterinarian duly licensed to practice his profession in this state. Upon
performing such inoculation, the veterinarian shall issue to the owner or
custodian a certificate showing such fact and shall also deliver to such owner
or custodian a metallic or other suitable tag to be attached to the collar or
harness of such dog, which tag shall also certify to the fact of inoculation
against rabies.
   C.   Duration Of Inoculation: The inoculation performed under the provisions
of subsection B of this section shall be effective until the expiration of the
calendar year in which the vaccination was performed or the expiration of such
period of time as may be promulgated by the department of agriculture, as
evidenced by the certificate of the veterinarian.
   D.   Tag Specifications: The tag issued under the provisions of subsection B
of this section shall be in such form as shall be determined by the department
of agriculture.
   E.   Exhibition Of Certificate: At any reasonable time upon request of any
member of the police department, the owner or custodian of any unmuzzled dog
shall exhibit his certificate, issued under the provisions of subsection B of
this section, showing the inoculation against rabies of any dog owned or
controlled by him. (Ord. 04-98, 5-11-1998)
4-2A-3: NUMBER OF DOGS RESTRICTED:
It shall be unlawful for a person to own, harbor, keep, or shelter more than
three (3) dogs over the age of four (4) months at a residence within the city.
(Ord. 01-2007, 3-12-2007)
4-2A-4: RESTRAINT OF DOGS:
The owner or custodian of a dog shall keep the dog under restraint at all times
and shall not permit such dog to be at large off the premises of the property
of the owner or custodian unless the dog is under "restraint" as defined in
section
4-2A-1 of this article. (Ord. 04-98, 5-11-1998; amd. 2017 Code)
4-2A-5: NUISANCE DOGS:
   A.   Noise: It shall be unlawful for a person to own or harbor any dog or
dogs that, by frequent or habitual howling, yelping, barking, screeching, or
other vocalization or otherwise, shall cause serious annoyance or disturbance
to persons in the vicinity. Any unabated series of howling, yelping, barking,
screeching, or other vocalization for ten (10) or more minutes shall be prima
facie evidence that causes such serious annoyance or disturbance to any person
in the vicinity complaining thereof. (Ord. 01-2007, 3-12-2007)
   B.   Damage To Property: Any dog which shall, in any manner, destroy or
injure any animal, plant, shrub, or other property not on the premises of its
owner or custodian is hereby declared to be a nuisance, and such dog may be
taken up and impounded and may be redeemed in the manner provided in subsection
4-2A-6D of this article. (Ord. 04-98, 5-11-1998; amd. Ord. 01-2007, 3-12-2007)
4-2A-6: IMPOUNDMENT AND REDEMPTION PROVISIONS:
   A.   Authority To Impound: It shall be the duty of officers of the city
police department to take up and impound, in such place as may be designated
and set apart for that purpose by the county board or the mayor and city
council, any dog found running at large or unlicensed in the city contrary to
any of the provisions of this article.
   B.   Place Of Impoundment: When dogs are found running at large or
unlicensed and their ownership is known to the police officers, such dogs may
be impounded at the pound by the county board or the mayor and city council, at
the discretion of such police officers, but the police officers shall cite the
owner of such dog to answer charges of violation of this article. (Ord. 04-98,
5-11-1998)
   C.   Notice Of Impoundment And Citation Issued: In case of impounding, and
where the owner or custodian of such dog is disclosed by any rabies inoculation
tag or license tag worn thereby, or is otherwise known to the officers
impounding same, the police department shall at once give notice by mail to
such owner or keeper, informing him of the impounding of his dog, and shall
cite the owner or custodian of such dog to answer charges of violation of this
article. (Ord. 04-98, 5-11-1998; amd. 2017 Code)
   D.   Redemption Of Impounded Dogs:
      1.   Any dog impounded under the provisions of this article shall, unless
sooner redeemed, be held for the period of seven (7) days in order to afford
opportunity to the owner or custodian thereof to redeem the same. Any such
owner or custodian desiring to redeem his impounded dog shall pay to the city
clerk the ordinary impounding fee and the cost of keeping such dog.
      2.   In case the dog has not been inoculated against rabies for the
current year, the owner shall also advance the fee required to have such dog
inoculated by a duly licensed veterinarian as he or she elects, and the
poundkeeper shall forthwith cause the dog to be duly inoculated against rabies.
No dog shall be released without having been inoculated for the current
calendar year or in accordance with the requirements of the department of
agriculture. Upon payment of the required charges, the dog shall thereupon be
released to the owner or custodian.
   E.   Destruction Of Unredeemed Dogs: Any impounded dog which shall not be
redeemed within seven (7) days may be humanely destroyed or otherwise disposed
of by the poundkeeper. (Ord. 04-98, 5-11-1998)
4-2A-7: ENFORCEMENT OFFICIAL:
It shall be the duty of the Athens chief of police to enforce the provisions of
this article. (Ord. 04-98, 5-11-1998)
4-2A-8: PENALTIES:
   A.   Any owner or custodian of a dog who violates or fails to comply with
the provisions of this article shall, upon conviction, be punishable by a fine
not to exceed one hundred dollars ($100.00) for the first offense, two hundred
dollars ($200.00) for the second offense, and three hundred dollars ($300.00)
for each subsequent offense.
   B.   If any dog running at large causes any person or domestic animal injury
or death or causes property damage to any private or public property, the owner
of said dog shall be assessed a fine of four hundred dollars ($400.00). The
assessment of the fine shall be automatic (and not subject to the discretion of
the animal control officer or other enforcement officer), and the owner subject
thereto shall be liable therefor on a strict liability basis. It shall not be a
defense to the offense or to the assessment of the fine that the owner of the
dog took reasonable steps to prevent the dog from running at large. (Ord. 04-
2009, 6-8-2009)
ARTICLE B.  PROHIBITED AND RESTRICTED ANIMALS
SECTION:
4-2B-1: Certain Animals Prohibited
4-2B-2: Excepted Domestic Animals
4-2B-3: Penalties
4-2B-1: CERTAIN ANIMALS PROHIBITED:
   A.   Prohibited Animals Enumerated:
      1.   It shall be unlawful for any person to own, use, keep or permit to
be at large within the city any of the following animals: bees, pigeons,
rabbits, horses, cattle, sheep, goats, ponies, mules, pigs, swine, hogs, ducks,
geese, chickens, minks, skunks, foxes, chinchillas, or any other livestock or
poultry or any wild or vicious animal dangerous to mankind. (Ord. 02-88, 5-2-
1988)
      2.   Any animals mentioned in subsection A1 of this section, in number
and kind, permitted within the limits of the city as a result of having been
kept within the city limits prior to and up to the effective date of ordinance
02-88 shall be hereafter proscribed from the city limits pursuant to this
subsection if said animals are removed from and/or cease to be kept in the city
limits for a period of nine (9) continuous months. (Ord. 10-88, 6-6-1988)
   B.   Impoundment Of Animals; Authority To Kill: Any animal mentioned in
subsection A1 of this section which is found at large within the city shall be
impounded, if possible; provided, however, that whenever any police officer
believes such animal endangers any person or property, such animal may be
killed by said officer. (Ord. 02-88, 5-2-1988)
   C.   Notice Of Violation: An owner or keeper violating the provisions of
this section shall be given notice of said violation and a ten (10) day
opportunity to comply herewith. (Ord. 02-88, 5-2-1988; amd. 2017 Code)
4-2B-2: EXCEPTED DOMESTIC ANIMALS:
   A.   Excepted Domestic Animals Enumerated And Defined: Notwithstanding
anything herein to the contrary, persons residing in a single- or multiple-
family dwelling may be permitted to keep rabbits, domestic fowl or chinchillas
(hereafter "domestic animals" and/or "excepted domestic animals"), so long as
the number of animals in each category does not exceed four (4) per family. The
term "domestic fowl" is defined as all animals included in the zoological class
Aves which include, but are not limited to, chickens, ducks, turkeys, guineas
and pigeons, but shall exclude roosters, emus, and ostriches.
   B.   Prohibitions:
      1.   No slaughtering of domestic animals is permitted within the
territorial limits of the city. (Ord. 08-2009, 8-10-2009)
      2.   It shall be unlawful for the person or persons owning, harboring, or
otherwise having in custody (including the property owners, jointly and
severally, of the premises upon which the domestic animals are kept) domestic
animals to permit a domestic animal to run at large within the city or to be
tethered upon any street, alley or public grounds in the city. (Ord. 08-2009,
8-10-2009; amd. 2017 Code)
   C.   Enclosures: The domestic animals shall be kept in a secure enclosure,
and such enclosure shall be no closer than twenty five feet (25') from the
nearest neighbor's residence.
   D.   Enforcement Official: The mayor, with the advice and consent of the
city council, shall designate and appoint a city public officer, the duties and
rights of whom shall be as follows:
      1.   To make an inventory of excepted domestic animals, ownership of the
excepted domestic animals and ownership of property where such excepted
domestic animals are kept and harbored.
      2.   To administer and enforce this section and, in the performance of
his or her duties, have the right to enter upon private property at any
reasonable time after notice for the purpose of making inquiry and inspection
to determine if a violation of this section exists. Entry shall be made so as
to cause the least possible inconvenience or disruption to any person in
possession of the premises. Denial of entry shall result in forfeiture to keep
or harbor excepted domestic animals. (Ord. 08-2009, 8-10-2009)
   E.   Notice Of Violation: Any person found by the public officer to be in
violation of this section shall be served a notice of such violation. The
notice shall be served by certified mail, return receipt requested. Refusal of
delivery shall be considered effective delivery of the notice. The notice shall
state the specific violation of this section and shall inform the person that
he shall have ten (10) days from the date of delivery of the notice to abate
the condition or conditions in violation of this section. Refusal or failure to
abate the condition or conditions shall be subject to a citation for city
ordinance violation subject to the fine(s) set forth in section
4-2B-3 of this article and shall be enforceable by the county circuit court.
(Ord. 08-2009, 8-10-2009; amd. 2017 Code)
4-2B-3: PENALTIES:
Violation of this article shall subject the owner and/or keeper to a fine of
not less than twenty five dollars ($25.00) nor more than three hundred dollars
($300.00) for each offense; and each day of a continuing offense shall
constitute a separate violation. In addition to any other penalties imposed
upon any person violating this article, such person shall also be liable for
the costs of impounding or killing such animal, if necessary. (Ord. 02-88, 5-2-
1988)
CHAPTER 3
MISCELLANEOUS OFFENSES
SECTION:
4-3-1: Damage To Public Property
4-3-2: Offenses Involving Alcoholic Beverages
4-3-3: Possession/Consumption And Transportation Of Cannabis
4-3-4: Possession Of Drug Paraphernalia
4-3-1: DAMAGE TO PUBLIC PROPERTY:
No person shall cut, injure, mark, damage or deface any public building, sewer,
water pipe, water meter or transponder, hydrant, or other city property,
fixture or personal property, or any tree, grass, shrub, or walk in any public
way or public park. Any person violating this section may be fined up to one
thousand dollars ($1,000.00) for each offense and, additionally, shall be
responsible for all costs to repair and/or replace the damage to its condition
prior to the damage occurring. (Ord. 02-2015, 4-13-2015)
4-3-2: OFFENSES INVOLVING ALCOHOLIC BEVERAGES:
   A.   Definitions: Words and phrases, when used in this section, shall have
the meanings respectively ascribed to them as stated in section
2-1-2 of this code. (2017 Code)
   B.   Offenses Enumerated:
      1.   Possession In Public: No person shall carry or possess, transport,
or have any alcoholic liquor on any public way or right of way (including, but
not limited to, public highways, streets, alleys, and/or sidewalks) except in
the original package and with the seal unbroken, within the corporate limits of
the city. (Ord. O-5-75, 9-9-1975)
      2.   Consumption On Public Property: Except as may be strictly permitted
by ordinance of the city, no person shall consume any alcoholic liquor on any
public property belonging to the city or on any public way or right of way
(including, but not limited to, public highways, streets, alleys, and/or
sidewalks) within the corporate limits of the city. (Ord. 02-2005, 2-14-2005)
   C.   Penalty And Other Remedies:
      1.   Whoever violates any of the provisions of this section shall, upon
conviction, be punishable by a fine of not less than fifty dollars ($50.00) nor
more than two hundred dollars ($200.00). (Ord. O-5-75, 9-9-1975)
      2.   Actions brought to enforce any fine, penalty, or forfeiture under
this section shall be brought in the corporate name of the city as plaintiff.
(Ord. O-5-75, 9-9-1975; amd. 2017 Code)
      3.   Fines for the violation of this section, when collected, shall be
paid into the city treasury. (Ord. O-5-75, 9-9-1975)
4-3-3: POSSESSION/CONSUMPTION AND TRANSPORTATION OF CANNABIS:
   A.   Definition: For the purpose of this section, cannabis includes
marijuana, hashish and other substances which are identified as including any
parts of the plant Cannabis sativa, whether growing or not; the seeds thereof;
the resin extracted from any part of such plant; and any compound, manufacture,
salt, derivative, and all other cannabinol derivatives, including its naturally
occurring or synthetically produced ingredients, whether produced directly or
indirectly by extraction, or independently by means of chemical synthesis or by
a combination of extraction and chemical synthesis; but shall not include the
mature stalks of such plant, fiber produced from such stalks, oil or cake made
from the seeds of such plant, any other compound, manufacture, salt,
derivative, mixture or preparation of such mature stalks (except the resin
extracted therefrom), fiber, oil or calm, or the sterilized seed of such plant
which is incapable of germination.
   B.   Possession Prohibited:
      1.   No person under the age of twenty one (21) shall knowingly possess
ten grams (10g) or less of any substance containing cannabis.
      2.   No person under the age of twenty one (21) shall knowingly possess
between ten grams (10g) and not more than thirty grams (30g) of any substance
containing cannabis.
      3.   Possession of more than thirty grams (30g) of cannabis:
         a.   It is unlawful for any Illinois resident to knowingly possess
more than thirty grams (30g) of cannabis flower, five grams of cannabis
concentrate, and five hundred (500) milligrams of THC contained in a cannabis-
infused product.
         b.   It is unlawful for any non-Illinois resident to knowingly possess
more than fifteen grams (15g) of cannabis flower, two and one-half grams (2.5g)
of cannabis concentrate, and two hundred fifty (250) milligrams of THC
contained in a cannabis-infused product.
   C.   Unlawful Use Of Cannabis: It is unlawful for any person to consume
cannabis in any public place, within a residence or housing that is federally
assured, or on property/place where one can be viewed by the public.
Furthermore use of cannabis is not permitted in the presence of minor children
even in a private residence.
   D.   No person shall use cannabis in a motor vehicle.
   E.   No person shall possess cannabis within a private motor vehicle unless
it is in a secured, sealed container.
   F.   Penalty: For every violation of this section, a minimum three hundred
dollar ($300.00) fine shall be imposed. A violation of subsection B2 shall
incur a minimum fine of four hundred dollars ($400.00). A violation of
subsection B3 shall incur a minimum fine of five hundred dollars ($500.00) All
fine monies shall be deposited into the city's drug fund account. (Ord. 09-
2016, 9-12-2016; amd. Ord. 07-2023, 9-11-2023)
4-3-4: POSSESSION OF DRUG PARAPHERNALIA:
   A.   Definitions: As used in this section, the following terms shall include
and have the following meanings:
    CANNABIS: Means and includes any substance defined as cannabis in section 3
of the Illinois cannabis control act, 720 Illinois Compiled Statutes 550/3.
   DRUG PARAPHERNALIA: Any object or device used, designed for use or intended
for use in unlawfully ingesting, smoking, administering, or storing cannabis.
Drug paraphernalia includes, but is not limited to:
      1.   Metal, wooden, plastic, glass, stone or ceramic pipes, with or
without screens.
      2.   Water pipes.
      3.   Carburetion tubes and devices.
      4.   Smoking and carburetion masks.
      5.   Roach clips.
      6.   Bongs.
      7.   One hitters.
   B.   Possession Prohibited: No person shall knowingly possess any item of
drug paraphernalia with the intent to use it for the purpose of unlawfully
ingesting, inhaling or otherwise introducing cannabis or a controlled substance
into the human body.
   C.   Penalty: For every violation of this section, a minimum three hundred
dollar ($300.00) fine shall be imposed. All fine monies shall be deposited into
the city's drug fund account. (Ord. 07-2016, 9-12-2016)
CHAPTER 4
MINORS
SECTION:
4-4-1: Curfew Regulations
4-4-2: Tobacco Prohibitions
4-4-1: CURFEW REGULATIONS:
   A.   Age And Hour Restrictions: A curfew for all persons seventeen (17)
years old and younger shall exist and hereby does exist under this section
within the city limits from ten o'clock (10:00) P.M. on Monday through
Thursday, inclusive, until six o'clock (6:00) A.M. the following day, and
eleven o'clock (11:00) P.M. on Friday, Saturday and Sunday until six o'clock
(6:00) A.M. the following day. (Ord. 13-99, 10-19-1999; amd. 2017 Code)
   B.   Prohibited Presence During Curfew Hours: When a curfew exists under
this section, it shall be unlawful for any person seventeen (17) years old or
younger to be outdoors within the city unless accompanied by an adult. (Ord.
13-99, 10-19-1999)
   C.   Violation; Penalty: Anyone found guilty of violating the curfew
regulations of this section shall be guilty of a misdemeanor, punishable by a
fine of not less than one hundred dollars ($100.00) nor more than five hundred
dollars ($500.00) for each offense. (Ord. 13-99, 10-19-1999; amd. 2017 Code)
4-4-2: TOBACCO PROHIBITIONS:
   A.   Definition: For the purpose of this section, "smokeless tobacco" means
any tobacco products that are suitable for dipping or chewing.
   B.   Prohibitions:
      1.   No person shall sell, buy for, distribute samples of or furnish any
cigar, cigarette, smokeless tobacco or tobacco in any of its forms to any minor
under eighteen (18) years of age.
      2.   No minor under eighteen (18) years of age shall possess, purchase or
attempt to purchase any cigar, cigarette, smokeless tobacco or tobacco in any
of its forms.
   C.   Penalties:
      1.   Whoever commits an offense set forth in this section shall be fined
not less than twenty five dollars ($25.00) nor more than two hundred fifty
dollars ($250.00).
      2.   Whoever commits an offense as set forth in subsection B1 of this
section shall be fined not less than two hundred fifty dollars ($250.00).
      3.   Any person who shall violate this section shall, on conviction
thereof, be punishable by a fine which may be reduced by no more than twenty
five percent (25%) by approved public or community service of not less than
eight (8) hours nor more than forty (40) hours for each violation. (Ord. 08-
2016, 9-12-2016)
CHAPTER 5
FIREWORKS
SECTION:
4-5-1: Definitions
4-5-2: Manufacture Restricted
4-5-3: Sales Prohibited
4-5-4: Display Requirements
4-5-5: Exceptions To Provisions
4-5-6: Violation; Penalty
4-5-1: DEFINITIONS:
The following words, phrases, and terms, whenever they occur in this chapter,
shall be interpreted as follows:
CHIEF: The chief of the Athens fire protection district.
CONSUMER DISTRIBUTOR: Any person who distributes, offers for sale, sells, or
exchanges for consideration consumer fireworks in Illinois to another
distributor or directly to any retailer or person for resale.
CONSUMER FIREWORKS: Those fireworks that must comply with the construction,
chemical composition, and labeling regulations of the U.S. consumer products
safety commission as set forth in 16 CFR parts 1500 and 1507, and classified as
fireworks UN0336 or UN0337 by the United States department of transportation
under 49 CFR 172.101. "Consumer fireworks" shall not include snake or glowworm
pellets; smoke devices, trick noisemakers known as "party poppers", "booby
traps", "snappers", "trick matches", "cigarette loads", and "auto burglar
alarms"; sparklers; toy pistols, toy canes, toy guns, or other devices in which
paper or plastic caps containing twenty five hundredths (0.25) grain or less of
explosive compound are used, provided they are so constructed that the hand
cannot come in contact with the cap when in place for the explosion; and toy
pistol paper or plastic caps that contain less than twenty hundredths (0.20)
grain of explosive mixture, the sale and use of which shall be permitted at all
times.
CONSUMER FIREWORKS DISPLAY OR CONSUMER DISPLAY: The detonation, ignition, or
deflagration of consumer fireworks to produce a visual or audible effect.
CONSUMER OPERATOR: An adult individual who is responsible for the safety,
setup, and discharge of the consumer fireworks display and who has completed
the training required in 425 Illinois Compiled Statutes 35/2.2.
CONSUMER RETAILER: Any person who offers for sale, sells, or exchanges for
consideration consumer fireworks in Illinois directly to any person with a
consumer display permit.
DISPLAY FIREWORKS: 1.3G or special effects fireworks or as further defined in
the pyrotechnic distributor and operator licensing act.
FLAME EFFECT: The detonation, ignition, or deflagration of flammable gases,
liquids, or special materials to produce a thermal, physical, visual or audible
effect before the public, invitees, or licensees, regardless of whether
admission is charged, in accordance with National Fire Protection Association
160 guidelines, and as may be further defined in the pyrotechnic operator
licensing act.
LEAD PYROTECHNIC OPERATOR: An individual who is responsible for the safety,
setup and discharge of the pyrotechnic display and who is licensed pursuant to
the pyrotechnic operator licensing act.
OSFM: The Illinois office of the state fire marshal.
1.3G FIREWORKS: Those fireworks used for professional outdoor displays and
classified as fireworks UN0333, UN0334, or UN0335 by the United States
department of transportation under 49 CFR 172.101.
PERMITTEE: Any person, firm or corporation, and/or agent of such person, firm
or corporation, who has been issued a permit for supervised displays of
fireworks in the city of Athens, Illinois.
PERSON: An individual, firm, corporation, association, partnership, company,
consortium, joint venture, or commercial entity.
PYROTECHNIC DISPLAY: The detonation, ignition, or deflagration of display
fireworks or flame effects to produce visual or audible effects of an
exhibitional nature before the public, invitees, or licensees, regardless of
whether admission is charged, and as may be further defined in the pyrotechnic
operator licensing act.
SPECIAL EFFECTS FIREWORKS: Pyrotechnic devices used for special effects by
professionals in the performing arts in conjunction with theatrical, musical,
or other productions that are similar to consumer fireworks in chemical
compositions and construction, but are not intended for consumer use and are
not labeled as such or identified as "intended for indoor use". "Special
effects fireworks" are classified as fireworks UN0431 or UN0432 by the United
States department of transportation under 49 CFR 172.101. (Ord. 02-2014, 6-24-
2014)
4-5-2: MANUFACTURE RESTRICTED:
The manufacture of fireworks within the city limits is prohibited except as
authorized under the laws of the state. (Ord. 02-2014, 6-24-2014)
4-5-3: SALES PROHIBITED:
No person shall offer for sale, distribute, or sell at retail any type of
fireworks within the city limits. The sale of sparklers on public property is
prohibited within the city limits. All violations of this section should be
reported to the city police department or to the OSFM. (Ord. 02-2014, 6-24-
2014; amd. 2017 Code)
4-5-4: DISPLAY REQUIREMENTS:
   A.   Permit For Displays:
      1.   Rules And Regulations Adopted: The city council may adopt reasonable
rules and regulations for the granting of permits for fireworks displays
pursuant to the provisions and rules of the Illinois pyrotechnic use act, 425
Illinois Compiled Statutes 35/0.01 et seq. (Ord. 02-2014, 6-24-2014; amd. 2017
Code)
      2.   Permit Required; Restrictions: No person shall possess, store, use
or explode any pyrotechnic or consumer fireworks within the city jurisdiction
without a valid fireworks display permit. No person under the age of twenty one
(21) years shall be eligible to be issued such a display permit. The city
council will grant permits only for pyrotechnic fireworks displays.
      3.   Application For Permit: Written application for a pyrotechnic
fireworks display permit shall be filed on the form jointly approved by the
chief and the city and shall be available in the office of the city clerk
during regular city business hours.
      4.   Insurance Required: Each applicant must show proof of liability
insurance in a sum not less than one million dollars ($1,000,000.00) with an
insurer authorized to do business in Illinois. The permittee shall be
responsible for all damages or injuries occurring as a result of any
pyrotechnic display permitted, the amount not limited to the insurance
provided.
      5.   Proof Of Licensure: All individuals applying for a pyrotechnic
fireworks display permit must include a copy of his or her lead pyrotechnic
operator license issued by the OSFM and a copy of his or her pyrotechnic
distributor license issued by the OSFM. Alternatively, the applicant must
provide proof that the pyrotechnic display services shall be provided by a
licensed pyrotechnic distributor and that the display shall be conducted by a
licensed lead operator and that both licenses have been issued by the OSFM.
(Ord. 02-2014, 6-24-2014)
      6.   Investigation And Inspection:
         a.   The city clerk shall forward all completed application forms to
the chief within five (5) working days of receipt. The chief shall investigate
or cause to be investigated each application to determine whether the display
is of the character and so located so as not to constitute an unreasonable
hazard to any person or property and complies with all requirements for
pyrotechnic fireworks displays as contained in the Illinois pyrotechnic use
act, 425 Illinois Compiled Statutes 35/0.01 et seq. (Ord. 02-2014, 6-24-2014;
amd. 2017 Code)
         b.   The chief shall inspect each display site and investigate or
cause to be investigated each application to determine whether the display is
of a character and so located so as to comply with the requirements of this
chapter.
      7.   Issuance Or Denial Of Permit:
         a.   Following the investigation and inspection of the display site,
if the chief determines that all requirements of this chapter are satisfied,
then the chief or his designee shall approve and issue the pyrotechnic
fireworks display permit. A copy of each permit shall be forwarded by the
office of the city clerk to the city chief of police not less than forty eight
(48) hours before the display.
         b.   In the event that the chief or his designee does not approve the
display permit, the applicant shall be informed by the chief or his designee in
writing of the reasons thereof.
         c.   The city has the authority to refuse to issue display permits at
any time and for any reason, and reserves the authority to choose that only
certain persons may apply for and receive pyrotechnic display permits.
      8.   Compliance With Permit: The possession and use of pyrotechnic
fireworks by the permittee shall be lawful only for the purpose and display as
contained in the pyrotechnic display permit.
      9.   Nontransferability Of Permit: No permit granted hereunder shall be
transferable. Only the permittee, pyrotechnic operator and pyrotechnic
distributor named on the permit shall be authorized to possess and display the
pyrotechnic fireworks.
   B.   Pyrotechnic Distributors And Operators:
      1.   Licenses Required: Any person who puts on a pyrotechnic display must
use or otherwise employ a licensed pyrotechnic distributor who must employ a
licensed lead operator who is present during any pyrotechnic display and acts
as a supervisor to all display assistants. A copy of the application for a
pyrotechnic distributor's license and the lead operator's license must be
obtained from the OSFM, and both licenses must be obtained prior to the display
site inspection, issuance of permit and purchase of pyrotechnic display
fireworks.
      2.   Assistants: All assistants to the lead operator must be eighteen
(18) years of age and must be registered with the OSFM.
   C.   Hours Of Display: No fireworks display shall be conducted before ten
o'clock (10:00) A.M. or after eleven o'clock (11:00) P.M., except where prior
approval is granted by the chief and the city for special programs.
   D.   Indoor Displays: All indoor pyrotechnic displays shall be conducted in
buildings protected by automatic sprinkler systems. All display sites for
indoor pyrotechnic displays must be inspected prior to the issuance of a permit
for such display. (Ord. 02-2014, 6-24-2014)
4-5-5: EXCEPTIONS TO PROVISIONS:
Nothing in this chapter shall be construed to prohibit the use of fireworks by
railroads or other transportation agencies for signal purposes or illumination,
or the sale or use of blank cartridges for a show or theater, or for use by
military forces of the state of Illinois, the United States, or authorized
emergency service agencies such as rescue squads or fire and police departments
of the city or other municipalities. (Ord. 02-2014, 6-24-2014)
4-5-6: VIOLATION; PENALTY:
Any person violating the provisions of this chapter shall be guilty of a class
A misdemeanor and, upon a finding of guilty, shall be punishable by a fine not
to exceed seven hundred fifty dollars ($750.00). (Ord. 02-2014, 6-24-2014)
CHAPTER 6
DISCRIMINATION IN HOUSING
SECTION:
4-6-1: Adoption Of Federal Regulations; Enforcement
4-6-2: Regulations Posted
4-6-3: Booklets And Forms Available
4-6-1: ADOPTION OF FEDERAL REGULATIONS; ENFORCEMENT:
The city hereby adopts by reference the rules and regulations regarding fair
housing issued by the department of housing and urban development and shall
enforce fair housing standards that comply with and/or in accordance with the
fair housing rules and regulations of the U.S. department of housing and urban
development. (Ord. 02-96, 5-13-1996)
4-6-2: REGULATIONS POSTED:
The city will cause to be posted, in the offices of the city and at other
places in the city hall, notices and fair housing posters advising the public
of the fair housing standards to be enforced in the city. (Ord. 02-96, 5-13-
1996)
4-6-3: BOOKLETS AND FORMS AVAILABLE:
Complaint forms and booklets will be made available to the public and will
remain on file in the city office for the benefit of the public, and the city
shall provide any member of the public complaining of discrimination in housing
sufficient complaint forms to complete the process of such complaints. (Ord.
02-96, 5-13-1996; amd. 2017 Code)
TITLE 5
TRAFFIC; PUBLIC WAYS AND PROPERTY
CHAPTER 1
TRAFFIC SCHEDULES
SECTION:
5-1-1: Through Streets; Stop And Yield Intersections
5-1-2: One-Way Streets And Alleys
5-1-3: Speed Limit
5-1-4: Parking
5-1-5: Truck Traffic; Vehicle Weight Limits
5-1-6: Signs Posted
5-1-7: Parking To Obstruct Prohibited
5-1-1: THROUGH STREETS; STOP AND YIELD INTERSECTIONS:
   A.   Through Streets: The driver of a vehicle shall stop at the entrance of
a through street and shall yield the right of way to other vehicles which have
entered the intersection or which are approaching so close on a through street
as to constitute an immediate hazard, unless directed otherwise by a traffic
officer or a traffic control signal. The following are declared through
streets: (Ord. 04-79, 6-5-1979)
County Highway 2, from the north city limit to the west line of Main Street.
Hargrave Street, from Illinois Route 29 to the east line of Main Street.
Jackson Street, from the east line of Lincoln Street (grade school) on the west
end to Main Street on the east.
Jackson Street, from West Barn Hollow Drive, eastwardly, to the west line of
Lincoln Street.
Main Street, from Little Street on the south to and including North Grand
Avenue on the north.
Springfield Street, from the north city limit to the north line of Hargrave
Street.
(Ord. 04-79, 6-5-1979; amd. 2017 Code)
   B.   Stop Intersections: The driver of a vehicle shall stop in obedience to
a stop sign at an intersection where a stop sign is erected pursuant to this
chapter, at one or more entrances thereto, and shall proceed cautiously,
yielding to the vehicles not so obliged to stop which are within the
intersection or approaching so close as to constitute an immediate hazard,
unless traffic at such intersection is controlled by a police officer on duty,
in which event, there shall be compliance with the direction of the police
officer. The following are declared stop intersections: (Ord. 04-79, 6-5-1979)
All streets intersecting with the through streets specified in subsection A of
this section.
Adams Street, northbound and southbound, at its intersection with Madison
Street.
Adams Street, southbound, at its intersection with Little Street.
Adams Street, westbound, at its intersection with Jackson Street.
Bitteroot Drive, southbound, at its intersection with Lynwood Drive.
Bunchberry Court, southbound, at its intersection with Lynwood Drive.
Circle Drive, at its intersection with County Highway 2.
Clover Court, southbound, at its intersection with Lynwood Drive.
Dottie Bednarko Drive at its intersection with County Highway 2.
Jackson Street, westbound, at its intersection with Lincoln Street.
Lincoln Street, northbound and southbound, at its intersection with Washington
Street.
Little Street and Main Street, in all directions at the four-way intersection.
Little Street, northbound, and Oak Grove Drive, westbound, at their
intersection.
Main Street and Hargrave Street, in all directions at the three-way
intersection.
Mill Street, at its intersection from both directions onto Little Street.
Polk Street, at its intersection with Eureka Street.
Polk Street, northbound and southbound, at its intersection with Jefferson
Street.
Polk Street, northbound and southbound, at its intersection with Madison
Street.
Primm Street, northbound and southbound, at its intersection with Madison
Street.
South Barn Hollow Drive, northbound, at its intersection with West Jackson
Street.
Washington Street, at its intersection with Mason Street.
Washington Street, eastbound and westbound, at its intersection with West
Street.
Washington Street, westbound, at its intersection with Wilson Road.
West Street, northbound, at its intersection with Washington Street.
(Ord. 04-79, 6-5-1979; amd. Ord. 07-95, 8-14-1995; Ord. 06-97, 9-8-1997; Ord.
06-99, 6-14-1999; Ord. 21-2002, 12-9-2002; Ord. 15-2003, 9-8-2003; Ord. 01-
2006, 1-9-2006; Ord. 10-2015, 10-12-2015; 2017 Code)
   C.   Yield Intersections: The city may, in its discretion and when traffic
conditions warrant such action, give preference to traffic upon any streets
under its jurisdiction over traffic crossing or entering such streets by
erecting appropriate yield signs. The driver of a vehicle shall yield the right
of way in obedience to a sign as required herein at an intersection and shall
proceed cautiously, yielding to all other vehicles which are within the
intersection or approaching so close as to constitute an immediate hazard, but
then may proceed. The following are declared yield intersections: (Ord. 04-79,
6-5-1979)
Cedar Street, northbound, at its intersection with Madison Street.
Jackson Street, eastbound, at its intersection with West Street.
Jefferson Street, at all streets intersecting Jefferson Street, except those
identified as stop intersections in subsection B of this section.
Madison Street, at all streets intersecting Madison Street.
Mill Street, at its intersection with Washington Street.
Polk Street, northbound, at its intersection with Washington Street.
(Ord. 04-79, 6-5-1979; amd. Ord. 15-2003, 9-8-2003; 2017 Code)
   D.   Enforcement:
      1.   Fine: Any person violating any provision of this section shall be
fined not less than twenty five dollars ($25.00) nor more than seven hundred
fifty dollars ($750.00) for each offense. (Ord. 07-95, 8-14-1995; amd. 2017
Code)
      2.   Traffic Violation Ticket: For offenses under this section, an
appropriate law enforcement officer may issue a traffic violation ticket
notifying the offender to appear in court at the time designated for hearing
such cases.
      3.   Failure To Appear; Arrest Warrant: A warrant for arrest may issue if
the offender does not appear at the time and place so specified. (Ord. 07-95,
8-14-1995)
5-1-2: ONE-WAY STREETS AND ALLEYS:
The following are one-way streets and alleys in the city:
   Webster alley, westbound, from Main Street to Adams Street.
(Ord. 01-85, 4-1-1985)
5-1-3: SPEED LIMIT:
   A.   Established; Exceptions:
      1.   The maximum speed limit on the streets within the city limits for
which the city has maintenance responsibility and are not under the
jurisdiction of either the department of transportation of the state of
Illinois or the highway commissioner of Menard County is twenty five (25) miles
per hour.
      2.   Nothing herein shall be determined to modify, alter or amend the
designation of any highway, street, part thereof or zone as a "school zone", as
provided in 625 Illinois Compiled Statutes 5/11-605, which has been heretofore
determined as a "school zone" by the Illinois department of transportation or
the city council. (Ord. 11-2015, 10-12-2015)
   B.   Enforcement:
      1.   Fine: Any person violating any provision of this section shall be
fined not less than the sentence for applicable speeding violations set forth
in the Illinois vehicle code in the Illinois Compiled Statutes.
      2.   Traffic Violation Ticket: For offenses under this section, an
appropriate law enforcement officer may issue a traffic violation ticket
notifying the offender to appear in court at the time designated for hearing
such cases.
      3.   Failure To Appear; Arrest Warrant: A warrant for arrest may issue if
the offender does not appear at the time and place so specified. (Ord. 07-2010,
9-13-2010)
5-1-4: PARKING:
   A.   No Parking Areas Designated: The mayor, in consultation with the city
council and the city police department, shall determine and designate certain
areas as "No Parking" areas by signs and/or such other markings notifying the
public that parking is not permitted in a particular space or area. Anyone
found guilty of parking in a designated "No Parking" space or area pursuant to
this subsection shall be guilty of a misdemeanor, punishable by a fine of
seventy five dollars ($75.00) for each offense. Each day that a person parks in
such designated space or area shall constitute a separate offense. (Ord. 02-
2001, 5-14-2001)
5-1-5: TRUCK TRAFFIC; VEHICLE WEIGHT LIMITS:
   A.   Weight Limits On Certain Streets:
      1.   No vehicle in excess of twenty eight thousand (28,000) pounds in
gross weight shall be permitted to travel upon North Main Street from the C&IM
Railroad tracks north to the city limits at North Grand Avenue. (Ord. 02-85, 4-
1-1985)
      2.   Whenever any vehicle is operated in violation of the provisions of
this section, the owner or driver of such vehicle may be prosecuted for such
violation. Any person, firm or corporation convicted of a violation hereunder
shall be fined for the first or second conviction an amount equal to or not
less than fifty dollars ($50.00) nor more than seven hundred fifty dollars
($750.00), and for the third and subsequent convictions by the same person,
firm or corporation, not less than seven hundred fifty dollars ($750.00) nor
more than one thousand dollars ($1,000.00). (Ord. 02-85, 4-1-1985; amd. 2017
Code)
5-1-6: SIGNS POSTED:
Signs shall be erected giving notice of the regulations of this chapter in
conformity with the standards and specifications as provided by statutes and
regulations. (2017 Code)
5-1-7: PARKING TO OBSTRUCT PROHIBITED:
   A.   No person shall stop, stand or park any vehicle upon any street in such
manner or under such conditions as to leave available less than ten feet (10')
of the width of the roadway for free movement of vehicular traffic, except that
a driver may stop temporarily during the actual loading or unloading of
passengers or when necessary in obedience to traffic regulations or traffic
signs or signals of a police officer.
   B.   Further, the following are declared obstructions to traffic:
      1.   The parking of a motor vehicle, camper, trailer, boat or other
personal property (hereinafter called "vehicle") upon any of the streets in the
City for longer than seventy two (72) hours consecutively without moving the
vehicle for use or cause, shall constitute an obstruction of the street.
   C.   A vehicle which constitutes an obstruction, as herein set forth, shall
he deemed to be in violation of the provisions of this chapter and is declared
to be a nuisance. It may be abated by any police officer following notice being
made to the owner or operator of the offending vehicle and allowing twenty-four
(24) hours for the owner or operator to remediate the offense following said
notice. If not properly addressed within the twenty four (24) hour period, any
police officer may impound such vehicle by removing and conveying such vehicle
or by causing such vehicle to be removed to a vehicle pound. A vehicle pound is
declared to be any suitable place designated by the police department of the
City as a vehicle pound. The owner or operator of said vehicle may have it
removed from such impoundment by paying the cost of towing and impounding of
the vehicle together with all fines and penalties as provided in this title.
The right to impound shall be in addition to any other remedy provided herein.
The registered owner of the vehicle at the time of the violation shall be
presumed to be the violator, as well as the vehicle itself, and the actual
operator thereof. Anyone found guilty of parking to obstruct pursuant to this
subsection shall be guilty of a misdemeanor, punishable by a fine of one
hundred dollars ($100.00) for each offense. (Ord. 2022-13, 12-12-2022)
CHAPTER 2
SKATEBOARDS, ROLLER SKATES AND SCOOTERS
SECTION:
5-2-1: Nuisances Declared
5-2-2: Violation; Penalty
5-2-1: NUISANCES DECLARED:
The following conduct shall be deemed public nuisances:

sidewalks within the city.
   B.   The use of skateboards, skates, or scooters, whether motorized or not,

Within the area with a western boundary on the west side of the Main Street
from the north side of Clinton Alley to the south side of Washington Street;
with a northern boundary on the south side of Washington Street from the west
side of Main Street to the east side of West Street; with an eastern boundary
on the east side of West Street from the north side of Washington Street to the
south side of Jefferson Street; and with a southern boundary on the south side
of Jefferson Street from the east side of West Street to the east side of Main
Street south to Clinton Alley then west to the west side of Main Street.
   C.   The use of skateboards, skates, or scooters, whether motorized or not,
in a manner that fails to yield to pedestrians. (Ord. 12-2003, 8-11-2003)

2003; amd. 2017 Code)
CHAPTER 3
GOLF CARTS AND RECREATIONAL VEHICLES
SECTION:
5-3-1: Definitions
5-3-2: Compliance With City And State Regulations
5-3-3: Driver's License And Age Requirements
5-3-4: Mandatory Insurance
5-3-5: Permit And Vehicle Requirements
5-3-6: Permitted And Prohibited Areas Of Operation
5-3-7: Hours Of Operation (Rep. by Ord. 11-2017, 10-9-2017)
5-3-8: Method Of Riding; Seat Belt Required
5-3-9: Driving Under The Influence Prohibited
5-3-10: Transporting Alcoholic Beverages
5-3-11: Certain Nonhighway Vehicles Prohibited
5-3-12: Nonliability Of City
5-3-13: Penalties
5-3-1: DEFINITIONS:
For the purpose of this chapter, the following words and terms, as used in this
chapter, shall have the meanings respectively ascribed to them in this section:
CITY: The City of Athens, Menard County, Illinois.
GOLF CART: A vehicle specifically designed and intended for the purposes of
transporting one or more persons and their golf clubs or maintenance equipment
while engaged in the playing of golf, supervising the play of golf, or
maintaining the condition of the grounds on a public or private golf course 1 .
A golf cart is further defined as a "nonhighway vehicle", as set forth in 625
Illinois Compiled Statutes 5/11-1426.1.
RECREATIONAL OFF HIGHWAY VEHICLE: Any motorized off highway device designed to
travel primarily off highway, sixty four inches (64") or less in width, having
a manufacturer's dry weight of two thousand (2,000) pounds or less traveling on
four (4) or more nonhighway tires, designed with a nonstraddle seat and a
steering wheel for steering control, except equipment such as lawn mowers.
STREETS AND ROADWAYS UNDER THE JURISDICTION OF THE CITY OF ATHENS: All those
streets and roadways located within the corporate boundaries of the City of
Athens, Illinois, and under the jurisdiction of the City of Athens, Menard
County, Illinois. (Ord. 01-2013, 3-11-2013)
 
Notes
1 1. 625 ILCS 5/1-123.9.
5-3-2: COMPLIANCE WITH CITY AND STATE REGULATIONS:
   A.   No person shall ride, drive, or operate any golf cart or recreational
off highway vehicle on any roadway or street located within the corporate limit
of the City except as specifically set forth in this chapter.
   B.   Every golf cart or recreational off highway vehicle operated as
authorized in this chapter shall comply with any and all traffic regulations
found in 625 Illinois Compiled Statutes 5/1-1 et seq. (Ord. 01-2013, 3-11-2013)
5-3-3: DRIVER'S LICENSE AND AGE REQUIREMENTS:
A person may not operate a golf cart or recreational off highway vehicle upon
the streets and roadways unless he/she has a valid Illinois driver's license
issued in his/her name by the Illinois Secretary of State, or a valid out of
State driver's license issued in his/her name by the appropriate department/
agency of the state responsible for issuing drivers' licenses and is at least
twenty one (21) years of age. (Ord. 01-2013, 3-11-2013; amd. 2017 Code)
5-3-4: MANDATORY INSURANCE:
Any person who operates a golf cart or recreational off highway vehicle shall
be subject to the mandatory insurance requirements under article 6 of chapter 7
of the Illinois Vehicle Code 1 , and shall provide proof of such insurance at
the time the permit is requested and at the time of each annual renewal. (Ord.
01-2013, 3-11-2013; amd. 2017 Code)
 
Notes
1 1. 625 ILCS 5/7-601 et seq.
5-3-5: PERMIT AND VEHICLE REQUIREMENTS:
No golf cart or recreational off highway vehicle shall be operated on the City
streets or roadways unless it is inspected and a permit is issued by the City.
The Chief of Police, and/or his designee, shall be in charge of the inspection.
The golf cart or recreational off highway vehicle being inspected must meet the
specifications as set forth in 625 Illinois Compiled Statutes 5/11-1426.1(e).
Those requirements are as follows: (Ord. 01-2013, 3-11-2013)
   A.   No "nonhighway vehicle" (golf cart or recreational off highway vehicle)
may be operated on a roadway unless, at a minimum, it has the following:
steering wheel apparatus, tires, rearview mirror, red reflectorized warning
devices in the front and rear, slow moving emblem, as required of other
vehicles in 625 Illinois Compiled Statutes 5/12-709, on the rear of the
"nonhighway vehicle" (golf cart or recreational off highway vehicle), headlight
that emits a white light visible from a distance of five hundred feet (500') to
the front, taillamp that emits a red light visible from at least one hundred
feet (100') from the rear, brake lights, and turn signals. (Ord. 01-2013, 3-11-
2013; amd. 2017 Code)
   B.   When operated on a street or roadway within the City, the golf cart or
recreational off highway vehicle shall have its headlights and taillamps
lighted as required by 625 Illinois Compiled Statutes 5/12-201 entitled "when
lighted lamps are required".
   C.   Provided the golf cart or recreational off highway vehicle passes
inspection and proof of insurance is provided, a permit shall be issued.
Permits shall be issued for a period of one year and will renew annually.
   D.   The cost of the permit will be fifty dollars ($50.00). The permit fee
shall be waived for all governmental or recognized not for profit entities.
   E.   A "nonhighway vehicle" (golf cart or recreational off highway vehicle)
must have a decal or registration approved by the City on the rear of the
vehicle and must have a copy of the permit issued by the City, valid
registration, and proof of valid insurance in the golf cart or recreational off
highway vehicle at all times and available for production at any time as
requested by any policing agency.
   F.   The City may issue a temporary special event permit for use of golf
carts or recreational off highway vehicles that may not be in compliance with
the requirements of this chapter and that is valid and issued only during that
event. (Ord. 01-2013, 3-11-2013)
5-3-6: PERMITTED AND PROHIBITED AREAS OF OPERATION:
   A.   1. Golf carts or recreational off highway vehicles shall only be
allowed to be operated on those streets and roadways upon which the City has
jurisdiction.
      2.   Golf carts or recreational off highway vehicles may not be operated
on Illinois State Route 29 or any other Illinois Department of Transportation
road.
      3.   Golf carts or recreational off highway vehicles shall not make a
direct crossing upon or across Illinois State Route 29 or any other Illinois
Department of Transportation road.
   B.   No person shall operate a golf cart or recreational off highway vehicle
upon any sidewalk located within the jurisdictional limits of the City.
   C.   No person shall operate a golf cart or recreational off highway vehicle
in the City parks other than parking areas.
   D.   The Street Superintendent shall cause appropriate signs to be posted on
those streets and roadways where golf carts or recreational off highway
vehicles are authorized to be operated pursuant to this chapter and the State
Statutes referenced herein. (Ord. 01-2013, 3-11-2013)
5-3-7: HOURS OF OPERATION:
(Rep. by Ord. 11-2017, 10-9-2017)
5-3-8: METHOD OF RIDING; SEAT BELT REQUIRED:
Any operator or passenger of a golf cart or recreational off highway vehicle
shall be in a sitting position and wearing a seat belt. (Ord. 01-2013, 3-11-
2013)
5-3-9: DRIVING UNDER THE INFLUENCE PROHIBITED:
Any person who drives or is in actual physical control of a golf cart or
recreational off highway vehicle on a roadway while under the influence is
subject to 625 Illinois Compiled Statutes 5/11-501 through 5/11-502. (Ord. 01-
2013, 3-11-2013; amd. 2017 Code)
5-3-10: TRANSPORTING ALCOHOLIC BEVERAGES:
   A.   Any person who drives or is in actual physical control of a golf cart
or recreational off highway vehicle on a roadway and who transports alcohol in
said golf cart or recreational off highway vehicle is subject to 625 Illinois
Compiled Statutes 5/11-502.
   B.   Any person who is a passenger in a golf cart or recreational off
highway vehicle on a roadway and who transports alcohol in said golf cart or
recreational off highway vehicle is subject to 625 Illinois Compiled Statutes
5/11-502. (Ord. 01-2013, 3-11-2013; amd. 2017 Code)
5-3-11: CERTAIN NONHIGHWAY VEHICLES PROHIBITED:
This chapter shall not be deemed to authorize any other nonhighway vehicles, as
defined in 625 Illinois Compiled Statutes 5/11-1426.1, to be operated on any
streets or roadways within the corporate boundaries of the City upon which the
City has jurisdiction (all-terrain vehicles or off highway motorcycles). (Ord.
01-2013, 3-11-2013)
5-3-12: NONLIABILITY OF CITY:
No action by the City under this chapter or 625 Illinois Compiled Statutes 5/
11-1426.1 designates the operation of a golf cart or recreational off highway
vehicle as an intended or permitted use of property with respect to section 3-
102 of the Local Governmental and Governmental Employees Tort Immunity Act.
(Ord. 01-2013, 3-11-2013)
5-3-13: PENALTIES:
Any person who violates any term or provision of this chapter shall be subject
to a fine, upon conviction, in an amount not less than seventy five dollars
($75.00) nor more than seven hundred fifty dollars ($750.00) for each separate
offense. Any second or subsequent offense shall result in the revocation of the
permit for a period of not less than one nor more than three (3) years. (Ord.
01-2013, 3-11-2013)
CHAPTER 4
PUBLIC LIBRARY
SECTION:
5-4-1: Library Established
5-4-2: Library Board Of Trustees
5-4-3: Library Tax
5-4-1: LIBRARY ESTABLISHED:
Pursuant to 75 Illinois Compiled Statutes 5/2-1, a public library is hereby
established and shall be maintained by the city. (Ord. 13-95, 11-13-1995)
5-4-2: LIBRARY BOARD OF TRUSTEES:
   A.   Appointment: Pursuant to 75 Illinois Compiled Statutes 5/4-1 and 5/4-
1.1, the mayor shall, with the approval of the city council, appoint a board of
nine (9) trustees chosen from residents of the city with reference to their
fitness for such office. Not more than one member of the city council shall be,
at any one time, a member of the library board of trustees.
   B.   Terms Of Office: The first library trustees of the city public library
shall hold office as follows: one-third (1/3) shall serve for one year, one-
third (1/3) for two (2) years, and one-third (1/3) for three (3) years, from
July 1 following their appointment. At their first regular meeting, those
trustees shall cast lots for the respective terms. Annually thereafter, the
mayor shall, before July 1 of each year, appoint as before three (3) trustees
to take the place of the retiring trustees. The trustees appointed shall hold
office for three (3) years and until their successors are appointed. (Ord. 13-
95, 11-13-1995)
5-4-3: LIBRARY TAX:
Pursuant to 75 Illinois Compiled Statutes 5/3-1, a tax in the amount of fifteen
hundredths percent (0.15%) of the value of all the taxable property in the
city, as equalized or assessed by the Illinois department of revenue, shall be
and hereby is levied for library purposes, the proceeds of which shall be paid
to the board of trustees of the library for expenditure for library purposes
under the direction of said board of trustees. (Ord. 13-95, 11-13-1995)
CHAPTER 5
EXCAVATIONS
SECTION:
5-5-1: Permit To Excavate
5-5-2: Cash Deposits, Liquidated Damages
5-5-3: Backfilling Excavation
5-5-4: Backfill Materials
5-5-5: Trench Surface Repair
5-5-6: Permanent Patch Materials
5-5-7: Detours
5-5-8: Excavations To Be Guarded
5-5-9: Installation Of Public Utilities
5-5-10: Maintenance Of Permanent Patch
5-5-11: Additional Repair Requirements
5-5-1: PERMIT TO EXCAVATE:
   A.   It shall be unlawful to make any opening or excavation into, across or
under any street, alley or public area within the corporate limits of the City
prior to obtaining a sewer tap/street break permit from the City Clerk. The
permit shall be issued after required fees and/or deposits are received by the
Public Works Department. At the time of filing for an excavation permit, the
application shall be accompanied by a certified check or money order, payable
to the City of Athens, to cover the cost of processing the application and
inspecting the excavation and restoration, in the amount of $75.
   B.   All public utilities having franchise agreements with the City shall be
exempted from obtaining a permit prior to commencing excavation for a utility
repair. However, said utility must submit, for each excavation, one copy of the
street break permit form to the Public Works Department within seven days after
commencing each excavation. The utility shall include the dimensions of the
excavation on the bottom of the street break permit form.
   C.   A violation of any of the provisions of this chapter shall subject the
offender to a penalty of not less than $75 nor more than the cost of repair on
a time and materials basis as outlined by the Public Works Director or their
designee for each offense, and the deposit, or such part thereof as may be
necessary to put said sheet in proper condition, and reimburse the City for
superintending the excavation and the refilling of same shall be forfeited to
the City.
