their operation may give rise to unique problems with respect to their impact
upon neighboring property or public facilities. (Ord., 10-11-1999)
8-3B-2: APPLICATION FOR SPECIAL USE:
Any person who has a freehold interest in land, or a possessory interest
entitled to exclusive possession, or a contractual interest which may become a
freehold interest, or an exclusive possessory interest which is specifically
enforceable may file an application to use land for a special use provided in
this title in the zoning district in which the land is located. An application
for a special use permit, including a planned residential development special
use permit, shall be filed with and on a form available from the zoning
administrator. The application shall be accompanied by such plans and/or data
prescribed by the zoning board, and shall include a statement in writing by the
applicant and adequate evidence showing that the proposed special use will
conform to the standards set forth in the guidelines for applicants. The fee
for such an application shall be as set out in section 8-3-5 of this chapter.
(Ord., 10-11-1999; amd. 2017 Code)
8-3B-3: HEARING AND NOTICE:
Upon receipt in proper form of the application and statement referred to in
this article, the zoning board shall hold at least one public hearing on the
proposed special use. Not more than thirty (30) days nor less than fifteen (15)
days in advance of such hearing, notice of the time and place of such hearing
shall be published in a newspaper of general circulation in the city, as
prescribed by applicable state statutes. Supplemental or additional notices may
be published or distributed as the zoning board may, by rule, prescribe from
time to time. (Ord., 10-11-1999; amd. 2017 Code)
8-3B-4: ZONING BOARD FINDINGS OF FACT AND RECOMMENDATIONS:
   A.   Within thirty (30) days after the close of the public hearing on a
special use permit application, the zoning board shall make written findings of
fact and shall submit same, together with its recommendations, to the city
council. The city council shall make findings based upon the evidence presented
to it in each specific case that: (Ord., 10-11-1999; amd. 2017 Code)
      1.   The establishment, maintenance or operation of the special use will
not be detrimental to or endanger the public health, safety, comfort or general
welfare.
      2.   The special use will not be injurious to the use and enjoyment of
other property in the immediate vicinity for the purpose already permitted, nor
substantially diminished or property values impaired within the neighborhood.
      3.   The establishment of the special use will not impede the normal and
orderly development and improvement of the surrounding property for uses
permitted in the district.
      4.   Adequate utilities, access roads, drainage and/or necessary
facilities have been or are being provided, to include curbing, if deemed
necessary by the city council, sewer and water lines to the property line,
subject to approval by the engineer, architect or such other expert as the city
deems necessary.
      5.   Adequate measures have been or will be taken to provide ingress and
egress so designed as to minimize traffic congestion in the public streets.
(Ord., 10-11-1999)
      6.   The special use shall, in all other respects, conform to the
applicable regulations of the district in which it is located except as such
regulations may, in each instance, be modified by the city council pursuant to
the recommendations of the zoning board.
   B.   For each application for a special use permit, the zoning board shall
report to the city council the stipulations or additional conditions and
guarantees to be complied with by the applicant when they are deemed necessary
for the protection of the public interest. (Ord., 10-11-1999; amd. 2017 Code)
8-3B-5: CITY COUNCIL ACTION:
Any action taken by the city council with regard to special uses shall be by
ordinance. (Ord., 10-11-1999)
CHAPTER 4
ZONING DISTRICTS AND MAP
SECTION:
8-4-1: Districts Established
8-4-2: Zoning Map
8-4-3: Boundaries Of Districts
8-4-4: Zoning Of Annexed Land
8-4-5: Compliance With District Regulations
8-4-1: DISTRICTS ESTABLISHED:
For the purpose of this title, all land within the corporate limits of the city
is hereby designated on the zoning district map as being in one of the
following districts:
 
R-1 Low density residential district
R-2 Medium density residential district
R-3 High density residential district
B-1 Business commercial district
M-1 Limited manufacturing district
A-1 Agricultural district
A-2 Recreational district
 
(Ord., 10-11-1999; amd. 2017 Code)
8-4-2: ZONING MAP:
The locations and boundaries of the districts established herein are shown on
the zoning district map which is hereby incorporated into this title. The
zoning district map, together with all notations, references, and other
information shown thereon, and all amendments thereto, shall be a part of this
title and shall have the same force and effect as if the zoning district map,
together with all notations, references and other information shown thereon,
were fully set forth and described herein. The zoning map referred to herein
and adopted as part of this title shall be identified as the "zoning district
map of the city of Athens, Illinois". (Ord., 10-11-1999)
8-4-3: BOUNDARIES OF DISTRICTS:
   A.   Unless otherwise indicated on the zoning district map, the boundary
lines of the districts follow lot lines and centerlines of streets, alleys,
waterways, and railroad rights of way, or such centerlines extended, or the
corporate limits existing at the effective date hereof.
   B.   Where the centerline of a street, alley, public way, waterway or
railroad right of way serves as a district boundary, the zoning of such areas,
unless otherwise specifically designated, shall be deemed to be the same.
Example: A railroad butting an R-1 residence district is then considered
residential. (Ord., 10-11-1999)
8-4-4: ZONING OF ANNEXED LAND:
It is the duty of the zoning board, prior to or at the time of annexation, to
establish the zoning classification for the territory proposed to be annexed.
Thereafter, the procedure utilized for the zoning of such territory should be
the same procedure provided for the adoption of amendments to the title, i.e.,
public notice and public hearing. (Ord., 10-11-1999; amd. 2017 Code)
8-4-5: COMPLIANCE WITH DISTRICT REGULATIONS:
No building or land shall hereafter be used and no building or part thereof
shall be erected, moved or altered unless for a use expressly permitted by and
in conformity with the regulations for the district in which it is located.
(Ord., 10-11-1999)
CHAPTER 5
RESIDENTIAL DISTRICTS
ARTICLE A.  R-1 LOW DENSITY RESIDENTIAL DISTRICT
SECTION:
8-5A-1: Permitted Principal Uses
8-5A-2: Permitted Accessory Uses
8-5A-3: Special Uses
8-5A-4: Dimensional Requirements
8-5A-5: Off Street Parking And Loading
8-5A-5-1: Purpose
8-5A-5-2: Application Of Provisions
8-5A-5-3: Plot Plan Required
8-5A-5-4: Off Street Parking Requirements
8-5A-5-5: Parking Trucks, Trailers And Heavy Equipment
8-5A-6: Special Requirements
8-5A-7: Fees
8-5A-1: PERMITTED PRINCIPAL USES:
 Accessory structures consistent with the principal use. (See definition of
"accessory use structure" in section
8-2-1 of this title.)
Private garages. (See definition of "garage, private" in section
8-2-1 of this title.)
Remodeling. (See definition of "remodeling" in section
8-2-1 of this title.)
Room additions. (See definition of "room addition" in section
8-2-1 of this title.)
Single-family detached dwellings.
Single-family detached modular homes. (Ord., 10-11-1999; amd. 2017 Code)
8-5A-2: PERMITTED ACCESSORY USES:
 Private recreational and hobby uses such as swimming pools, tennis courts and
gardens. (Ord., 10-11-1999)
8-5A-3: SPECIAL USES:
Churches, schools, libraries, parks, playgrounds and community centers.
Daycare centers.
Home occupations. (See definition of "home occupation" in section
8-2-1 of this title.)
Home residence bed and breakfast operations. (See definition of "home residence
bed and breakfast operation" in section
8-2-1 of this title.)
Signs. (See definition of "sign" in section
8-2-1 of this title.)
Utility substations and pump houses. (Ord., 10-11-1999; amd. 2017 Code)
8-5A-4: DIMENSIONAL REQUIREMENTS:
(See definition of "lot" in section
8-2-1 of this title.)
A. Lot area:            
   Minimum           5,000 square feet
B. Lot width:           
   Minimum           50 feet
C. Lot frontage:        
   Minimum           50 feet
D. Yard requirements:   
   Minimum:           
    Front           20 feet
    Rear            20 feet
    Side            10 feet
    Corner          20 feet (corner is at intersecting roads)
E. Height:              
   Maximum           35 feet
F. Off street parking:  
   Minimum           2 spaces per unit
 
(Ord., 10-11-1999)
8-5A-5: OFF STREET PARKING AND LOADING:
8-5A-5-1: PURPOSE:
This section
8-5A-5 is provided to increase safety and lessen congestion in the public
streets, to adequately provide for parking needs associated with the
development of land and increased automobile usage, to set standards for the
requirement of off street parking according to the amount of traffic generated
by each use, and to reduce the on street storage of vehicles. (Ord., 10-11-
1999)
8-5A-5-2: APPLICATION OF PROVISIONS:
   A.   Generally: For all buildings and structures erected and all uses of
land established after the effective date hereof, accessory parking and loading
facilities shall be provided as required by the regulations of the district in
which such buildings or uses are located. However, where a building permit has
been issued prior to the effective date hereof, and provided, that construction
is begun within ninety (90) days of such effective date, and diligently
prosecuted to completion, parking and loading facilities as required
hereinafter need not be provided.
   B.   Increase In Intensity Of Use: When the intensity of use of any
building, structure or premises shall be increased through the addition of
dwelling units, gross floor area, seating capacity or other units of
measurement specified herein for required parking or loading facilities,
parking and loading facilities as required herein shall be provided for such
increase in intensity of use. However, no building or structure lawfully
erected or use lawfully established prior to the effective date hereof shall be
required to provide such additional parking or loading facilities unless and
until the aggregated increase in units of measurement shall equal not less than
fifteen percent (15%) of the units of measurement existing upon said effective
date.
   C.   Change Of Use: Whenever the existing use of a building or structure
shall hereafter be changed to a new use, parking or loading facilities shall be
provided as required for such new use. However, if the said building or
structure was erected prior to the effective date hereof, additional parking or
loading facilities are mandatory only in the amount by which the requirements
for the new use would exceed those for the existing use if the latter were
subject to the parking and loading provisions of this section
8-5A-5.
   D.   Accessory Parking And Loading Facilities: Accessory off street parking
or loading facilities which are located on the same lot as the building or use
served and which were in existence on the effective date hereof or were
provided voluntarily after such effective date shall not hereafter be reduced
below, or if already less than, shall not further be reduced below the
requirements of this section
8-5A-5 for a similar new building or use.
   E.   Damage Or Destruction Of Building Or Use: For any conforming or legally
nonconforming building or use which is in existence on the effective date
hereof which, subsequent thereto, is damaged or destroyed by fire, collapse,
explosion or other cause, and which is reconstructed, reestablished, or
repaired, off street parking or loading facilities equivalent to any maintained
at the time of such damage or destruction shall be restored or continued in
operation. However, in no case shall it be necessary to restore or maintain
parking or loading facilities in excess of those required by this section
8-5A-5 for equivalent new uses or construction. (Ord., 10-11-1999)
8-5A-5-3: PLOT PLAN REQUIRED:
Any application for a building permit, or for a certificate of occupancy where
no building permit is required, shall include therewith a plot plan, drawn to
scale and fully dimensioned, showing any parking or loading facilities to be
provided in compliance with this section
8-5A-5. (Ord., 10-11-1999)
8-5A-5-4: OFF STREET PARKING REQUIREMENTS:
   A.   Design Requirements:
      1.   Stall And Aisle Dimensions: All required spaces shall conform to the
following stall and aisle dimensions:
 
Parking Angle Stall Width Width Of Stall    Depth Of Stall         Aisle Width
                          Parallel To Aisle Perpendicular To Aisle
45°          10'         14'14"            20'                    11'6"
60°          10'         11'5"             20'                    18'
90°          10'         10'               20'                    29'
 
      2.   Access: Each required off street parking space shall open directly
upon an aisle or driveway of such width and design as to provide safe and
efficient means of vehicular access to such parking space. All off street
parking facilities shall be designed with appropriate means of vehicular access
to a street or alley in a manner which will least interfere with traffic
movements. No driveway across public property nor curb cut shall exceed a width
of thirty feet (30').
      3.   Screening: All open automobile parking areas containing more than
four (4) parking spaces shall be effectively screened on each side adjoining or
fronting on any property situated in a residential district or any
institutional premises by a wall, fence or densely planted compact hedge not
less than five feet (5') nor more than seven feet (7') in height. Such required
screening shall conform with the front and side yard setback requirements of
the district in which the parking is located.
   B.   Off Premises Parking: If off street parking space for nonresidential
uses as required in section
8-5A-5-2 of this chapter cannot be provided on the same lot on which the
principal use is conducted, the zoning administrator may permit such space to
be provided on other off street property, provided such space is within four
hundred feet (400') of the main entrance to such principal use. Such off street
parking space shall thereafter be deemed to be required open space associated
with the permitted use and shall not be reduced nor encroached upon in any
manner.
   C.   Joint Use Of Facilities: If groups of buildings contain uses which vary
in their parking requirements, the number of parking spaces shall be the sum of
the individual requirements for each use. However, where peak parking
requirements occur at distinctly different times of the day or at different
times of the week as determined by the zoning administrator, joint parking
facilities may be shared by two (2) or more uses.
   D.   Maintenance Of Facilities:
      1.   All parking facilities and accessways to the parking areas shall be
maintained in a dust free condition; parking areas located between a public
street and the principal building on the lot shall be maintained in a dust free
condition.
      2.   Accessways between public streets and property lines shall be
maintained with a substance similar to the composition of the street.
      3.   Any lighting shall be arranged and maintained so that it does not
shine directly upon any adjacent dwelling or street and does not produce
excessive glare.
      4.   Uncovered parking spaces must be at least three feet (3') from any
street right of way line.
   E.   Number Of Spaces:
      1.   The following number of surfaced off street automobile parking
spaces shall be provided for the following permitted accessory uses and special
uses:
         a.   Churches shall have one parking space per four (4) seating spaces
in the main sanctuary.
         b.   Schools shall have parking spaces as follows:
            (1)   Elementary and junior high schools shall have two (2) parking
spaces per three (3) teachers and other employees;
            (2)   Senior high schools, colleges, and universities shall have
two (2) parking spaces per three (3) teachers and other employees, plus one
parking space per five (5) students;
            (3)   Nursery schools shall have two (2) parking spaces per three
(3) teachers and other employees, plus one off street loading space per eight
(8) pupils; and
            (4)   If a school has an auditorium or assembly hall which may be
used by persons other than students of the school, the parking requirements set
forth under subsection 8-6-5-4E1 of this title, entry reading "theaters,
auditoriums and places of assembly", shall be used to fulfill the parking
requirements of the school, provided the parking spaces are located near both
uses.
      2.   For uses not listed in subsection E1 of this section, parking spaces
shall be provided on the same basis as required for the most similar listed
use, or as determined by the zoning administrator.
      3.   When determination of the number of off street parking spaces
required by this subsection E results in a requirement of a fractional space,
any fraction of one-half (1/2) or less may be disregarded while a fraction in
excess of one-half (1/2) shall be counted as one parking space. (Ord., 10-11-
1999)
8-5A-5-5: PARKING TRUCKS, TRAILERS AND HEAVY EQUIPMENT:
In all residential districts, not more than one truck with a gross weight of
eight thousand (8,000) pounds or less, one trailer with a gross weight of five
thousand (5,000) pounds or less and not more than one boat and/or boat trailer
may be parked in a building or in a rear yard but not in a required front or
side yard unless said parking is on an improved surface and covers only that
portion of the yard that leads to parking space in the side or rear yard.
Furthermore, no heavy vehicular equipment in excess of eight thousand (8,000)
pounds shall be parked in a residential district. (Ord., 10-11-1999)
8-5A-6: SPECIAL REQUIREMENTS:
   A.   Adequate Access: See definition of "adequate access" in section
8-2-1 of this title.
   B.   Projections Into Yards:
      1.   Architectural Features: Architectural features of residential
buildings, such as windowsills, cornices, and roof overhangs, may project into
the required yard, provided such projections are not closer than four feet (4')
to any lot line.
      2.   Residential Structures Projecting Into Front Yards: Any residential
structure may project into the required front yard of existing residential
structures on both adjacent lots in the same district having less than the
required minimum front yard; provided, however, that such projection extends no
closer to the street than either of the adjacent structures.
   C.   Location Of Certain Structures And Items:
      1.   Accessory Structures: No accessory structure shall be constructed
closer than twenty feet (20') to the front and rear lot lines and ten feet
(10') off the side lot lines and a driveway not closer than two feet (2') along
a lot line.
      2.   Mechanical Devices: No mechanical device designed for the purpose of
controlling the internal environment of the structure shall be permitted in any
front yard or within eight feet (8') of any lot line.
      3.   Ground Mounted Satellite Antennas: No ground mounted dish type
satellite signal receiving antennas, also referred to as earth stations or
ground stations, shall be permitted in any front yard or street frontage or
within eight feet (8') of any lot line. (Ord., 10-11-1999)
   D.   Location Of Parking Areas: Required parking spaces shall not be located
in the required front yard unless said parking is on an improved surface or
that portion of the yard that leads to the parking space in the side or rear
yard. (Ord., 10-11-1999; amd. 2017 Code)
   E.   Storage Required In Enclosed Structures:
      1.   Contractor Equipment And Tools: All contractor earthmoving equipment
and/or tools shall be parked or stored in a completely enclosed structure on
all residential premises except when making a delivery or rendering a service
at such premises. (Ord., 10-11-1999)
      2.   Unlicensed Or Inoperable Vehicles: All unlicensed and/or inoperable
motor vehicles shall be parked or stored in a completely enclosed, roofed
building on all residential premises. (Ord. 09-2006, 10-9-2006)
   F.   Visibility Of Intersections:
      1.   See definition of "intersections" in section
8-2-1 of this title.
      2.   For landscaping on any corner lot, surface grading shall be such as
to permit unobstructed vision between the heights of two and one-half (21/2)
and ten feet (10') within the sight triangle formed by the center of the
intersection and two (2) points fifty feet (50') distant, each point being on
the centerline of an intersection street.
   G.   Culverts: No culverts will be installed until approved by the city. The
homeowner will pay for the first culvert which will be maintained by the city
thereafter.
   H.   Fences, Walls And Hedges:
      1.   Fences, walls and hedges are permitted in a required side or rear
yard along a lot line, provided they do not exceed six feet (6') in height.
      2.   Fences, walls and hedges are permitted in any front yard along a lot
line; provided, that a solid fence, wall or hedge does not exceed two and one-
half feet (21/2') in height and a fence, wall or hedge which has visibility
through it (for example, a chainlink fence) does not exceed four feet (4') in
height.
      3.   Fences, walls and hedges shall not be closer than two feet (2')
along a lot line when next to a driveway.
   I.   Swimming Pools: See definition of "swimming pools" in section
8-2-1 of this title.
   J.   Fallout Shelters: See definition of "fallout shelters" in section
8-2-1 of this title.
   K.   Tents: See definition of "tents" in section
8-2-1 of this title.
   L.   Drainage Tile: See definition of "drainage tile" in section
8-2-1 of this title. (Ord., 10-11-1999; amd. 2017 Code)
8-5A-7: FEES:
See section 8-3-5 of this title. (Ord., 10-11-1999)
ARTICLE B.  R-2 MEDIUM DENSITY RESIDENTIAL DISTRICT

(Ord., 10-11-1999; amd. 2017 Code)
8-5B-5: OFF STREET PARKING AND LOADING:
8-5B-5-1: PURPOSE:
This section
8-5B-5 is provided to increase safety and lessen congestion in the public
streets, to adequately provide for parking needs associated with the
development of land and increased automobile usage, to set standards for the
requirement of off street parking according to the amount of traffic generated
by each use, and to reduce the on street storage of vehicles. (Ord., 10-11-
1999)
8-5B-5-2: APPLICATION OF PROVISIONS:
   A.   Generally: For all buildings and structures erected and all uses of
land established after the effective date hereof, accessory parking and loading
facilities shall be provided as required by the regulations of the district in
which such buildings or uses are located. However, where a building permit has
been issued prior to the effective date hereof, and provided, that construction
is begun within ninety (90) days of such effective date, and diligently
prosecuted to completion, parking and loading facilities as required
hereinafter need not be provided.
   B.   Increase In Intensity Of Use: When the intensity of use of any
building, structure or premises shall be increased through the addition of
dwelling units, gross floor area, seating capacity or other units of
measurement specified herein for required parking or loading facilities,
parking and loading facilities as required herein shall be provided for such
increase in intensity of use. However, no building or structure lawfully
erected or use lawfully established prior to the effective date hereof shall be
required to provide such additional parking or loading facilities unless and
until the aggregated increase in units of measurement shall equal not less than
fifteen percent (15%) of the units of measurement existing upon said effective
date.
   C.   Change Of Use: Whenever the existing use of a building or structure
shall hereafter be changed to a new use, parking or loading facilities shall be
provided as required for such new use. However, if the said building or
structure was erected prior to the effective date hereof, additional parking or
loading facilities are mandatory only in the amount by which the requirements
for the new use would exceed those for the existing use if the latter were
subject to the parking and loading provisions of this section
8-5B-5.
   D.   Accessory Parking And Loading Facilities: Accessory off street parking
or loading facilities which are located on the same lot as the building or use
served and which were in existence on the effective date hereof or were
provided voluntarily after such effective date shall not hereafter be reduced
below, or if already less than, shall not further be reduced below the
requirements of this section
8-5B-5 for a similar new building or use.
   E.   Damage Or Destruction Of Building Or Use: For any conforming or legally
nonconforming building or use which is in existence on the effective date
hereof which, subsequent thereto, is damaged or destroyed by fire, collapse,
explosion or other cause, and which is reconstructed, reestablished, or
repaired, off street parking or loading facilities equivalent to any maintained
at the time of such damage or destruction shall be restored or continued in
operation. However, in no case shall it be necessary to restore or maintain
parking or loading facilities in excess of those required by this section
8-5B-5 for equivalent new uses or construction. (Ord., 10-11-1999)
8-5B-5-3: PLOT PLAN REQUIRED:
Any application for a building permit, or for a certificate of occupancy where
no building permit is required, shall include therewith a plot plan, drawn to
scale and fully dimensioned, showing any parking or loading facilities to be
provided in compliance with this section
8-5B-5. (Ord., 10-11-1999)

F. Off street parking:  
   Minimum           2 spaces per unit, adjacent to the dwelling unit served
 
(Ord., 10-11-1999)
8-5C-5: OFF STREET PARKING AND LOADING:
8-5C-5-1: PURPOSE:
This section
8-5C-5 is provided to increase safety and lessen congestion in the public
streets, to adequately provide for parking needs associated with the
development of land and increased automobile usage, to set standards for the
requirement of off street parking according to the amount of traffic generated
by each use, and to reduce the on street storage of vehicles. (Ord., 10-11-
1999)
8-5C-5-2: APPLICATION OF PROVISIONS:
   A.   Generally: For all buildings and structures erected and all uses of
land established after the effective date hereof, accessory parking and loading
facilities shall be provided as required by the regulations of the district in
which such buildings or uses are located. However, where a building permit has
been issued prior to the effective date hereof, and provided, that construction
is begun within ninety (90) days of such effective date, and diligently
prosecuted to completion, parking and loading facilities as required
hereinafter need not be provided.
   B.   Increase In Intensity Of Use: When the intensity of use of any
building, structure or premises shall be increased through the addition of
dwelling units, gross floor area, seating capacity or other units of
measurement specified herein for required parking or loading facilities,
parking and loading facilities as required herein shall be provided for such
increase in intensity of use. However, no building or structure lawfully
erected or use lawfully established prior to the effective date hereof shall be
required to provide such additional parking or loading facilities unless and
until the aggregated increase in units of measurement shall equal not less than
fifteen percent (15%) of the units of measurement existing upon said effective
date.
   C.   Change Of Use: Whenever the existing use of a building or structure
shall hereafter be changed to a new use, parking or loading facilities shall be
provided as required for such new use. However, if the said building or
structure was erected prior to the effective date hereof, additional parking or
loading facilities are mandatory only in the amount by which the requirements
for the new use would exceed those for the existing use if the latter were
subject to the parking and loading provisions of this section
8-5C-5.
   D.   Accessory Parking And Loading Facilities: Accessory off street parking
or loading facilities which are located on the same lot as the building or use
served and which were in existence on the effective date hereof or were
provided voluntarily after such effective date shall not hereafter be reduced
below, or if already less than, shall not further be reduced below the
requirements of this section
8-5C-5 for a similar new building or use.
   E.   Damage Or Destruction Of Building Or Use: For any conforming or legally
nonconforming building or use which is in existence on the effective date
hereof which, subsequent thereto, is damaged or destroyed by fire, collapse,
explosion or other cause, and which is reconstructed, reestablished, or
repaired, off street parking or loading facilities equivalent to any maintained
at the time of such damage or destruction shall be restored or continued in
operation. However, in no case shall it be necessary to restore or maintain
parking or loading facilities in excess of those required by this section
8-5C-5 for equivalent new uses or construction. (Ord., 10-11-1999)
8-5C-5-3: PLOT PLAN REQUIRED:
Any application for a building permit, or for a certificate of occupancy where
no building permit is required, shall include therewith a plot plan, drawn to
scale and fully dimensioned, showing any parking or loading facilities to be
provided in compliance with this section
8-5C-5. (Ord., 10-11-1999)
8-5C-5-4: OFF STREET PARKING REQUIREMENTS:
   A.   Design Requirements:
      1.   Stall And Aisle Dimensions: All required spaces shall conform to the
following stall and aisle dimensions:
 
Parking Angle Stall Width Width Of Stall    Depth Of Stall         Aisle Width
                          Parallel To Aisle Perpendicular To Aisle
45°          10'         14'14"            20'                    11'6"
60°          10'         11'5"             20'                    18'
90°          10'         10'               20'                    29'
 
      2.   Access: Each required off street parking space shall open directly
upon an aisle or driveway of such width and design as to provide safe and
efficient means of vehicular access to such parking space. All off street
parking facilities shall be designed with appropriate means of vehicular access
to a street or alley in a manner which will least interfere with traffic
movements. No driveway across public property nor curb cut shall exceed a width
of thirty feet (30').
      3.   Screening: All open automobile parking areas containing more than
four (4) parking spaces shall be effectively screened on each side adjoining or
fronting on any property situated in a residential district or any
institutional premises by a wall, fence or densely planted compact hedge not
less than five feet (5') nor more than seven feet (7') in height. Such required
screening shall conform with the front and side yard setback requirements of
the district in which the parking is located.
   B.   Off Premises Parking: If off street parking space for nonresidential
uses as required in section
8-5C-5-2 of this chapter cannot be provided on the same lot on which the
principal use is conducted, the zoning administrator may permit such space to
be provided on other off street property, provided such space is within four
hundred feet (400') of the main entrance to such principal use. Such off street
parking space shall thereafter be deemed to be required open space associated
with the permitted use and shall not be reduced nor encroached upon in any
manner.
   C.   Joint Use Of Facilities: If groups of buildings contain uses which vary
in their parking requirements, the number of parking spaces shall be the sum of
the individual requirements for each use. However, where peak parking
requirements occur at distinctly different times of the day or at different
times of the week as determined by the zoning administrator, joint parking
facilities may be shared by two (2) or more uses.
   D.   Maintenance Of Facilities:
      1.   All parking facilities and accessways to the parking areas shall be
maintained in a dust free condition; parking areas located between a public
street and the principal building on the lot shall be maintained in a dust free
condition.
      2.   Accessways between public streets and property lines shall be
maintained with a substance similar to the composition of the street.
      3.   Any lighting shall be arranged and maintained so that it does not
shine directly upon any adjacent dwelling or street and does not produce
excessive glare.
      4.   Uncovered parking spaces must be at least three feet (3') from any
street right of way line.
   E.   Number Of Spaces:
      1.   The following number of surfaced off street automobile parking
spaces shall be provided for the following permitted accessory uses and special
uses:
         a.   Churches shall have one parking space per four (4) seating spaces
in the main sanctuary.
         b.   Schools shall have parking spaces as follows:
            (1)   Elementary and junior high schools shall have two (2) parking
spaces per three (3) teachers and other employees;
            (2)   Senior high schools, colleges, and universities shall have
two (2) parking spaces per three (3) teachers and other employees, plus one
parking space per five (5) students;
            (3)   Nursery schools shall have two (2) parking spaces per three
(3) teachers and other employees, plus one off street loading space per eight
(8) pupils; and
            (4)   If a school has an auditorium or assembly hall which may be
used by persons other than students of the school, the parking requirements set
forth under subsection 8-6-5-4E1 of this title, entry reading "theaters,
auditoriums and places of assembly", shall be used to fulfill the parking
requirements of the school, provided the parking spaces are located near both
uses.
      2.   For uses not listed in subsection E1 of this section, parking spaces
shall be provided on the same basis as required for the most similar listed
use, or as determined by the zoning administrator.
      3.   When determination of the number of off street parking spaces
required by this subsection E results in a requirement of a fractional space,
any fraction of one-half (1/2) or less may be disregarded while a fraction in
excess of one-half (1/2) shall be counted as one parking space. (Ord., 10-11-
1999)
8-5C-5-5: PARKING TRUCKS, TRAILERS AND HEAVY EQUIPMENT:
In all residential districts, not more than one truck with a gross weight of
eight thousand (8,000) pounds or less, one trailer with a gross weight of five
thousand (5,000) pounds or less and not more than one boat and/or boat trailer
may be parked in a building or in a rear yard but not in a required front or
side yard unless said parking is on an improved surface and covers only that
portion of the yard that leads to parking space in the side or rear yard.
Furthermore, no heavy vehicular equipment in excess of eight thousand (8,000)
pounds shall be parked in a residential district. (Ord., 10-11-1999)
8-5C-6: SPECIAL REQUIREMENTS:
   A.   Adequate Access: See definition of "adequate access" in section
8-2-1 of this title.
   B.   Projections Into Yards:
      1.   Architectural Features: Architectural features of residential
buildings, such as windowsills, cornices, and roof overhangs, may project into
the required yard, provided such projections are not closer than three feet
(3') to any lot line.
      2.   Residential Structures Projecting Into Front Yards: Any residential
structure may project into the required front yard of existing residential
structures on both adjacent lots in the same district having less than the
required minimum front yard; provided, however, that such projection extends no
closer to the street than either of the adjacent structures. (Ord., 10-11-1999)
   C.   Location Of Certain Structures And Items:
      1.   Accessory Structures: No accessory structure shall be constructed
closer than twenty feet (20') to the front and rear lot lines and ten feet
(10') off the side lot lines and a driveway not closer than two feet (2') along
a lot line.
      2.   Mechanical Devices: No mechanical device designed for the purpose of
controlling the internal environment of the structure shall be permitted in any
front yard or within five feet (5') of any lot line. (Ord., 10-11-1999; amd.
2017 Code)
      3.   Ground Mounted Satellite Antennas: No ground mounted dish type
satellite signal receiving antennas, also referred to as earth stations or
ground stations, shall be permitted in any front yard or street frontage or
within eight feet (8') of any lot line. (Ord., 10-11-1999)
   D.   Location Of Parking Areas: Required parking spaces shall not be located
in the required front yard unless said parking is on an improved surface and
covers only that portion of the yard that leads to the parking space in the
side or rear yard. (Ord., 10-11-1999; amd. 2017 Code)
   E.   Storage Required In Enclosed Structures:
      1.   Contractor Equipment And Tools: All contractor earthmoving equipment
and/or tools shall be parked or stored in a completely enclosed structure on
all residential premises except when making a delivery or rendering a service
at such premises. (Ord., 10-11-1999)
      2.   Unlicensed, Inoperable Vehicles: All unlicensed or inoperable motor
vehicles shall be parked or stored in a completely enclosed, roofed building on
all residential premises. (Ord., 10-11-1999; amd. 2017 Code)
   F.   Visibility Of Intersections:
      1.   See definition of "intersections" in section
8-2-1 of this title.
      2.   For landscaping on any corner lot, surface grading shall be such as
to permit unobstructed vision between the heights of two and one-half (21/2)
and ten feet (10') within the sight triangle formed by the center of the
intersection and two (2) points fifty feet (50') distant, each point being on
the centerline of an intersection street.
   G.   Culverts: No culverts will be installed until approved by the city. The
homeowner will pay for the first culvert which will be maintained by the city
thereafter.
   H.   Fences, Walls And Hedges:
      1.   Fences, walls and hedges are permitted in a required side or rear
yard along a lot line, provided they do not exceed six feet (6') in height.
      2.   Fences, walls and hedges are permitted in any front yard along a lot
line; provided, that a solid fence, wall or hedge does not exceed two and one-
half feet (21/2') in height and a fence, wall or hedge which has visibility
through it (for example, a chainlink fence) does not exceed four feet (4') in
height.
      3.   Fences, walls and hedges shall not be closer than two feet (2')
along a lot line when next to a driveway.
   I.   Swimming Pools: See definition of "swimming pools" in section
8-2-1 of this title.
   J.   Fallout Shelters: See definition of "fallout shelters" in section
8-2-1 of this title.
   K.   Tents: See definition of "tents" in section
8-2-1 of this title.
   L.   Drainage Tile: See definition of "drainage tile" in section
8-2-1 of this title.
   M.   Fire Protection: Fire alarms, smoke detectors and fire exits must
comply with the state fire marshal regulations. (Ord., 10-11-1999)
8-5C-7: FEES:
See section 8-3-5 of this title. (Ord., 10-11-1999)

Remodeling. (See definition of "remodeling" in section

Room additions. (See definition of "room addition" in section

repair, photography studios, and laundry and dry cleaning establishments.

Other uses of similar scale and intensity to the above uses. (Ord., 10-11-1999;

 Automobile service stations.
Home residence bed and breakfast operations. (See definition of "home residence
bed and breakfast operation" in section

Hotels.
Not for profit clubs and lodges, fraternal or religious institutions.
Production of goods for sale on the premises, such as bakeries, printing, etc.
Public and private parking lots and garages.
Residential dwelling units above the first floor; owner occupied dwelling units
on the first floor. (Ord., 10-11-1999; amd. 2017 Code)

(Ord., 10-11-1999; amd. 2017 Code)
8-6-5: OFF STREET PARKING AND LOADING:

This section
8-6-5 is provided to increase safety and lessen congestion in the public
streets, to adequately provide for parking needs associated with the
development of land and increased automobile usage, to set standards for the
requirement of off street parking according to the amount of traffic generated
by each use, and to reduce the on street storage of vehicles. (Ord., 10-11-
1999)
8-6-5-2: APPLICATION OF PROVISIONS:
   A.   Generally: For all buildings and structures erected and all uses of
land established after the effective date hereof, accessory parking and loading
facilities shall be provided as required by the regulations of the district in
which such buildings or uses are located. However, where a building permit has
been issued prior to the effective date hereof, and provided, that construction
is begun within ninety (90) days of such effective date, and diligently
prosecuted to completion, parking and loading facilities as required
hereinafter need not be provided.
   B.   Increase In Intensity Of Use: When the intensity of use of any
building, structure or premises shall be increased through the addition of
dwelling units, gross floor area, seating capacity or other units of
measurement specified herein for required parking or loading facilities,
parking and loading facilities as required herein shall be provided for such
increase in intensity of use. However, no building or structure lawfully
erected or use lawfully established prior to the effective date hereof shall be
required to provide such additional parking or loading facilities unless and
until the aggregated increase in units of measurement shall equal not less than
fifteen percent (15%) of the units of measurement existing upon said effective
date.
   C.   Change Of Use: Whenever the existing use of a building or structure
shall hereafter be changed to a new use, parking or loading facilities shall be
provided as required for such new use. However, if the said building or
structure was erected prior to the effective date hereof, additional parking or
loading facilities are mandatory only in the amount by which the requirements
for the new use would exceed those for the existing use if the latter were
subject to the parking and loading provisions of this section
8-6-5.
   D.   Accessory Parking And Loading Facilities: Accessory off street parking
or loading facilities which are located on the same lot as the building or use
served and which were in existence on the effective date hereof or were
provided voluntarily after such effective date shall not hereafter be reduced
below, or if already less than, shall not further be reduced below the
requirements of this section
8-6-5 for a similar new building or use.
   E.   Damage Or Destruction Of Building Or Use: For any conforming or legally
nonconforming building or use which is in existence on the effective date
hereof which, subsequent thereto, is damaged or destroyed by fire, collapse,
explosion or other cause, and which is reconstructed, reestablished, or
repaired, off street parking or loading facilities equivalent to any maintained
at the time of such damage or destruction shall be restored or continued in
operation. However, in no case shall it be necessary to restore or maintain
parking or loading facilities in excess of those required by this section
8-6-5 for equivalent new uses or construction. (Ord., 10-11-1999)
8-6-5-3: PLOT PLAN REQUIRED:
Any application for a building permit, or for a certificate of occupancy where
no building permit is required, shall include therewith a plot plan, drawn to
scale and fully dimensioned, showing any parking or loading facilities to be
provided in compliance with this section
8-6-5. (Ord., 10-11-1999)
8-6-5-4: OFF STREET PARKING REQUIREMENTS:
   A.   Design Requirements:
      1.   Stall And Aisle Dimensions: All required spaces shall conform to the
following stall and aisle dimensions:
 
                          Width Of       Depth Of Stall

      2.   Access: Each required off street parking space shall open directly
upon an aisle or driveway of such width and design as to provide safe and
efficient means of vehicular access to such parking space. All off street
parking facilities shall be designed with appropriate means of vehicular access
to a street or alley in a manner which will least interfere with traffic
movements. No driveway across public property nor curb cut shall exceed a width
of thirty feet (30').
      3.   Screening: All open automobile parking areas containing more than

less than five feet (5') nor more than seven feet (7') in height. Such required
screening shall conform with the front and side yard setback requirements of
the district in which the parking is located.
   B.   Off Premises Parking: If off street parking space for nonresidential
uses as required in section
8-6-5-2 of this chapter cannot be provided on the same lot on which the
principal use is conducted, the zoning administrator may permit such space to

parking space shall thereafter be deemed to be required open space associated
with the permitted use and shall not be reduced nor encroached upon in any
manner.

in their parking requirements, the number of parking spaces shall be the sum of
the individual requirements for each use. However, where peak parking
requirements occur at distinctly different times of the day or at different
times of the week as determined by the zoning administrator, joint parking
facilities may be shared by two (2) or more uses.
   D.   Maintenance Of Facilities:
      1.   All parking facilities and accessways to the parking areas shall be
maintained in a dust free condition; parking areas located between a public
street and the principal building on the lot shall be maintained in a dust free
condition.
      2.   Accessways between public streets and property lines shall be
maintained with a substance similar to the composition of the street.
      3.   Any lighting shall be arranged and maintained so that it does not
shine directly upon any adjacent dwelling or street and does not produce
excessive glare.
      4.   Uncovered parking spaces must be at least three feet (3') from any
street right of way line.
   E.   Number Of Spaces:

spaces shall be provided for the following particular uses: (Ord., 10-11-1999)

      3.   When determination of the number of off street parking spaces
required by this subsection E results in a requirement of a fractional space,
any fraction of one-half (1/2) or less may be disregarded while a fraction in
excess of one-half (1/2) shall be counted as one parking space. (Ord., 10-11-
1999)
8-6-5-5: OFF STREET LOADING REQUIREMENTS:
   A.   Location: All required loading berths shall be located on the same
zoning lot as the use served. No loading berth for vehicles over two (2) tons'
capacity shall be closer than fifty feet (50') to a property in a residential
district unless completely enclosed by building walls or a uniformly painted
solid fence or wall, or any combination thereof, not less than six feet (6') in
height. No permitted or required loading berth shall be located within twenty
five feet (25') of the nearest point of the intersection of any two (2)
streets.
   B.   Design Requirements:
      1.   Space Dimensions: Unless otherwise specified, a required loading
berth shall be at least ten feet (10') in width by at least twenty five feet
(25') in length, exclusive of aisles and maneuvering space, and shall have a
vertical clearance of at least fourteen feet (14').
      2.   Access: Each required off street loading berth shall be designed
with appropriate means of vehicular access to a street or alley in a manner
which will least interfere with traffic movements.
      3.   Surface Specifications: All open off street leading berths shall be
improved with a compacted macadam base, not less than seven inches (7") thick,
surfaced with not less than two inches (2") of asphaltic concrete or some
comparable all weather, dustless material.
   C.   Use Restrictions:
      1.   No motor vehicle repair work or service of any kind shall be
permitted in conjunction with loading facilities provided in any residence or
business district.
      2.   Space allocated to any off street loading berth shall not, while so
allocated, be used to satisfy the space requirements for any off street parking
facilities or portions thereof.
   D.   Number Of Spaces: Off street loading berths shall be provided on the
basis of gross floor area of buildings, or portions thereof, devoted to such
use. All required off street loading berths shall conform to the following
schedule:
 
Square Feet Of Floor Area Minimum Number And Size Of Each Berth
   5,000 to 25,000     1 - 10 feet x 25 feet
   25,000 to 250,000   1 - 10 feet x 50 feet
 
(Ord., 10-11-1999)
8-6-6: SPECIAL REQUIREMENTS:
   A.   Adequate Access: See definition of "adequate access" in section
8-2-1 of this title.
   B.   Enclosed Businesses, Service, Storage, Etc.:
      1.   All business, service, storage, merchandise display repair and
processing is to be conducted within a completely enclosed building. Other uses
clearly incidental but necessary and appropriate to the principal use shall be
permitted beyond the limits of an enclosed building. Examples of these uses
include sidewalk sales, drive-in banking facilities and outdoor restaurants.
(Ord., 10-11-1999)
      2.   All contractor earthmoving equipment and/or tools, or unlicensed or
inoperable motor vehicles shall be parked or stored in a completely enclosed
structure on all residential premises except when making a delivery or
rendering a service at such premises. (Ord., 10-11-1999; amd. 2017 Code)
   C.   Outdoor Storage Restrictions: Outdoor storage in the business
commercial district shall be permitted only upon the approval by the city
council. All outdoor storage, when permitted, shall be no more than ten feet
(10') in height and shall be completely screened from public view. (Ord., 10-
11-1999)
   D.   Screening Adjacent To Residential Districts: Business commercial
districts adjacent to a residential district shall provide a dense hedge, tree
row or other suitable landscape device on that adjacent property line. All
landscaping must be approved by the city council as adequate to visually screen
the commercial area from the residential area. (Ord., 10-11-1999; amd. 2017
Code)
   E.   Location Of Ground Mounted Satellite Dishes: No ground mounted dish
type satellite signal receiving antennas, also referred to as earth stations or
ground stations, shall be permitted in any front yard or street frontage or
within eight feet (8') of any lot line.
   F.   First Floor Apartments: First floor apartment dwelling units may not
occupy more than the rear fifty percent (50%) of the main floor area and must
be separated from the business area by a permanent wall. The dwelling shall not
be visible from the street and must contain complete cooking and sanitation
facilities.
   G.   Visibility Of Intersections:
      1.   See definition of "intersections" in section
8-2-1 of this title.
      2.   For landscaping on any corner lot, surface grading shall be such as
to permit unobstructed vision between the heights of two and one-half (21/2)
and ten feet (10') within the sight triangle formed by the center of the
intersection and two (2) points fifty feet (50') distant, each point being on
the centerline of an intersection street.
   H.   Fences, Walls And Hedges:
      1.   Fences, walls and hedges are permitted in a required side or rear
yard along a lot line, provided they do not exceed six feet (6') in height.
      2.   Fences, walls and hedges are permitted in any front yard along a lot
line; provided, that a solid fence, wall or hedge does not exceed two and one-
half feet (21/2') in height and a fence, wall or hedge which has visibility
through it (for example, a chainlink fence) does not exceed four feet (4') in
height.
      3.   Fences, walls and hedges shall not be closer than two feet (2')
along a lot line when next to a driveway.
   I.   Fallout Shelters: See definition of "fallout shelters" in section
8-2-1 of this title.
   J.   Swimming Pools: See definition of "swimming pools" in section
8-2-1 of this title.
   K.   Tents: See definition of "tents" in section
8-2-1 of this title.
   L.   Drainage Tile: See definition of "drainage tile" in section
8-2-1 of this title. (Ord., 10-11-1999)
   M.   Dry Cleaning Establishments: Dry cleaning and pressing establishments
are permitted, when employing facilities for the cleaning and pressing of dry
goods received on the premises from retail trade only and not including any
wholesale cleaning or pressing business; and when using carbon tetrachloride,
perchlorethylene, or other similar nonflammable solvents approved by the fire
department. (Ord., 10-11-1999; amd. 2017 Code)
   N.   Junkyards Prohibited: All junkyards are prohibited. (Ord., 10-11-1999)
8-6-7: FEES:
See section
8-3-5 of this title. (Ord., 10-11-1999)

8-7-5: OFF STREET PARKING AND LOADING:
8-7-5-1: PURPOSE:
This section
8-7-5 is provided to increase safety and lessen congestion in the public
streets, to adequately provide for parking needs associated with the
development of land and increased automobile usage, to set standards for the
requirement of off street parking according to the amount of traffic generated
by each use, and to reduce the on street storage of vehicles. (Ord., 10-11-
1999)
8-7-5-2: APPLICATION OF PROVISIONS:
   A.   Generally: For all buildings and structures erected and all uses of
land established after the effective date hereof, accessory parking and loading
facilities shall be provided as required by the regulations of the district in
which such buildings or uses are located. However, where a building permit has
been issued prior to the effective date hereof, and provided, that construction
is begun within ninety (90) days of such effective date, and diligently
prosecuted to completion, parking and loading facilities as required
hereinafter need not be provided.
   B.   Increase In Intensity Of Use: When the intensity of use of any
building, structure or premises shall be increased through the addition of
dwelling units, gross floor area, seating capacity or other units of
measurement specified herein for required parking or loading facilities,
parking and loading facilities as required herein shall be provided for such
increase in intensity of use. However, no building or structure lawfully
erected or use lawfully established prior to the effective date hereof shall be
required to provide such additional parking or loading facilities unless and
until the aggregated increase in units of measurement shall equal not less than
fifteen percent (15%) of the units of measurement existing upon said effective
date.
   C.   Change Of Use: Whenever the existing use of a building or structure
shall hereafter be changed to a new use, parking or loading facilities shall be
provided as required for such new use. However, if the said building or
structure was erected prior to the effective date hereof, additional parking or
loading facilities are mandatory only in the amount by which the requirements
for the new use would exceed those for the existing use if the latter were
subject to the parking and loading provisions of this section
8-7-5.
   D.   Accessory Parking And Loading Facilities: Accessory off street parking
or loading facilities which are located on the same lot as the building or use
served and which were in existence on the effective date hereof or were
provided voluntarily after such effective date shall not hereafter be reduced
below, or if already less than, shall not further be reduced below the
requirements of this section
8-7-5 for a similar new building or use.
   E.   Damage Or Destruction Of Building Or Use: For any conforming or legally
nonconforming building or use which is in existence on the effective date
hereof which, subsequent thereto, is damaged or destroyed by fire, collapse,
explosion or other cause, and which is reconstructed, reestablished, or
repaired, off street parking or loading facilities equivalent to any maintained
at the time of such damage or destruction shall be restored or continued in
operation. However, in no case shall it be necessary to restore or maintain
parking or loading facilities in excess of those required by this section
8-7-5 for equivalent new uses or construction. (Ord., 10-11-1999)
8-7-5-3: PLOT PLAN REQUIRED:
Any application for a building permit, or for a certificate of occupancy where
no building permit is required, shall include therewith a plot plan, drawn to
scale and fully dimensioned, showing any parking or loading facilities to be
provided in compliance with this section
8-7-5. (Ord., 10-11-1999)
8-7-5-4: OFF STREET PARKING REQUIREMENTS:
   A.   Design Requirements:
      1.   Stall And Aisle Dimensions: All required spaces shall conform to the
following stall and aisle dimensions:
 
                          Width Of       Depth Of Stall
Parking Angle Stall Width Stall Parallel Perpendicular  Aisle Width
                          To Aisle       To Aisle
45°          10'         14'14"         20'            11'6"
60°          10'         11'5"          20'            18'
90°          10'         10'            20'            29'
 
      2.   Access: Each required off street parking space shall open directly
upon an aisle or driveway of such width and design as to provide safe and
efficient means of vehicular access to such parking space. All off street
parking facilities shall be designed with appropriate means of vehicular access
to a street or alley in a manner which will least interfere with traffic
movements. No driveway across public property nor curb cut shall exceed a width
of thirty feet (30').
      3.   Screening: All open automobile parking areas containing more than
four (4) parking spaces shall be effectively screened on each side adjoining or
fronting on any property situated in a residential district or any
institutional premises by a wall, fence or densely planted compact hedge not
less than five feet (5') nor more than seven feet (7') in height. Such required
screening shall conform with the front and side yard setback requirements of
the district in which the parking is located.
   B.   Off Premises Parking: If off street parking space for nonresidential
uses as required in section
8-7-5-2 of this chapter cannot be provided on the same lot on which the
principal use is conducted, the zoning administrator may permit such space to
be provided on other off street property, provided such space is within four
hundred feet (400') of the main entrance to such principal use. Such off street
parking space shall thereafter be deemed to be required open space associated
with the permitted use and shall not be reduced nor encroached upon in any
manner.
   C.   Joint Use Of Facilities: If groups of buildings contain uses which vary
in their parking requirements, the number of parking spaces shall be the sum of
the individual requirements for each use. However, where peak parking
requirements occur at distinctly different times of the day or at different
times of the week as determined by the zoning administrator, joint parking
facilities may be shared by two (2) or more uses.
   D.   Maintenance Of Facilities:
      1.   All parking facilities and accessways to the parking areas shall be
maintained in a dust free condition; parking areas located between a public
street and the principal building on the lot shall be maintained in a dust free
condition.
      2.   Accessways between public streets and property lines shall be
maintained with a substance similar to the composition of the street.
      3.   Any lighting shall be arranged and maintained so that it does not
shine directly upon any adjacent dwelling or street and does not produce
excessive glare.
      4.   Uncovered parking spaces must be at least three feet (3') from any
street right of way line. (Ord., 10-11-1999; amd. 2017 Code)
8-7-5-5: OFF STREET LOADING REQUIREMENTS:
   A.   Location: All required loading berths shall be located on the same
zoning lot as the use served. No loading berth for vehicles over two (2) tons'
capacity shall be closer than fifty feet (50') to a property in a residential
district unless completely enclosed by building walls or a uniformly painted
solid fence or wall, or any combination thereof, not less than six feet (6') in
height. No permitted or required loading berth shall be located within twenty
five feet (25') of the nearest point of the intersection of any two (2)
streets.
   B.   Design Requirements:
      1.   Space Dimensions: Unless otherwise specified, a required loading
berth shall be at least ten feet (10') in width by at least twenty five feet
(25') in length, exclusive of aisles and maneuvering space, and shall have a
vertical clearance of at least fourteen feet (14').
      2.   Access: Each required off street loading berth shall be designed
with appropriate means of vehicular access to a street or alley in a manner
which will least interfere with traffic movements.
      3.   Surface Specifications: All open off street leading berths shall be
improved with a compacted macadam base, not less than seven inches (7") thick,
surfaced with not less than two inches (2") of asphaltic concrete or some
comparable all weather, dustless material.
   C.   Use Restrictions:
      1.   No motor vehicle repair work or service of any kind shall be
permitted in conjunction with loading facilities provided in any residence or
business district.
      2.   Space allocated to any off street loading berth shall not, while so
allocated, be used to satisfy the space requirements for any off street parking
facilities or portions thereof.
   D.   Number Of Spaces: Off street loading berths shall be provided on the
basis of gross floor area of buildings, or portions thereof, devoted to such
use. All required off street loading berths shall conform to the following
schedule:
 
Square Feet Of Floor Area Minimum Number And Size Of Each Berth
5,000 to 25,000           1 - 10 feet x 25 feet
25,000 to 250,000         1 - 10 feet x 50 feet
 
(Ord., 10-11-1999)
8-7-6: SPECIAL REQUIREMENTS:
   A.   Adequate Access: See definition of "adequate access" in section
8-2-1 of this title.
   B.   Enclosed Businesses And Storage Of Certain Items:
      1.   All metal fabrication, welding, and cutting shall be done in an
enclosed building. (Ord., 10-11-1999)
      2.   All contractor earthmoving equipment and/or tools or unlicensed or
inoperable motor vehicles shall be parked or stored in a completely enclosed
structure on all residential premises except when making a delivery or
rendering a service at such premises.
   C.   Outdoor Storage Restrictions: Outdoor storage in the limited
manufacturing district shall be permitted only upon the approval by the city
zoning board and/or the city council. All outdoor storage, when permitted,
shall be no more than ten feet (10') in height and shall be completely screened
from public view.
   D.   Screening Adjacent To Residential Or Commercial Districts: Limited
manufacturing districts adjacent to residential or commercial districts shall
provide a dense hedge, tree row or other suitable landscape device on that
adjacent property line. All landscaping must be approved by the zoning board
and/or the city council as adequate to visually screen the manufacturing zone
from residential or commercial areas. (Ord., 10-11-1999; amd. 2017 Code)
   E.   Location Of Ground Mounted Satellite Dishes: No ground mounted dish
type satellite signal receiving antennas, also referred to as earth stations or
ground stations, shall be permitted in any front yard or street frontage, or
within eight feet (8') of any lot line.
   F.   Adequate Ventilation: All buildings shall be equipped with adequate
ventilation.
   G.   Visibility Of Intersections:
      1.   See definition of "intersections" in section
8-2-1 of this title.
      2.   For landscaping on any corner lot, surface grading shall be such as
to permit unobstructed vision between the heights of two and one-half (21/2)
and ten feet (10') within the sight triangle formed by the center of the
intersection and two (2) points fifty feet (50') distant, each point being on
the centerline of an intersection street.
   H.   Fences, Walls And Hedges:
      1.   Fences, walls and hedges are permitted in a required side or rear
yard along a lot line, provided they do not exceed six feet (6') in height.
      2.   Fences, walls and hedges are permitted in any front yard along a lot
line; provided, that a solid fence, wall or hedge does not exceed two and one-
half feet (21/2') in height and a fence, wall or hedge which has visibility
through it (for example, a chainlink fence) does not exceed four feet (4') in
height.
      3.   Fences, walls and hedges shall not be closer than two feet (2')
along a lot line when next to a driveway.
   I.   Fallout Shelters: See definition of "fallout shelters" in section
8-2-1 of this title.
   J.   Swimming Pools: See definition of "swimming pools" in section
8-2-1 of this title.
   K.   Tents: See definition of "tents" in section
8-2-1 of this title.
   L.   Drainage Tile: See definition of "drainage tile" in section
8-2-1 of this title.
   M.   Junkyards Prohibited: All junkyards are prohibited. (Ord., 10-11-1999)
8-7-7: FEES:
See section
8-3-5 of this title. (Ord., 10-11-1999)

CHAPTER 10
NONCONFORMITIES
SECTION:
8-10-1: Continuance Of Nonconforming Buildings And Uses
8-10-2: Structures Under Construction
8-10-3: Nonconforming Buildings And Structures
8-10-4: Nonconforming Uses Of Buildings And Structures
8-10-5: Nonconforming Use Of Land
8-10-1: CONTINUANCE OF NONCONFORMING BUILDINGS AND USES:
   A.   Any lawfully established use of a building or land on the effective
date hereof or amendments hereto that does not conform to the use regulations
for the district in which it is located shall be deemed to be a legal
nonconforming use and may be continued, except as otherwise provided herein.
   B.   Any legal, nonconforming building or structure may be continued in use,
provided there is no physical change other than necessary maintenance and
repair, except as otherwise permitted herein. (Ord., 10-11-1999)
8-10-2: STRUCTURES UNDER CONSTRUCTION:
   A.   Any building for which a permit has been lawfully granted prior to the
effective date hereof or of amendments hereto may be completed in accordance
with the approved plans, provided construction is started within one hundred
(100) days and diligently prosecuted to completion. Such building shall
thereafter be deemed a lawfully established building. (Ord., 10-11-1999)
   B.   All construction, both exterior and interior, that is to be performed
pursuant to a duly issued building permit shall be completed no later than one
year from the issuance of the building permit. The failure to complete such
construction within such time shall constitute a revocation of the building
permit and shall result in the uncompleted building being a nonconforming
building, subjecting the owner to all applicable penalties for such
nonconforming use, including fines and injunctive relief. The one year
completion requirement for all construction commenced pursuant to building
permits issued prior to the effective date of this subsection shall commence on
the effective date of this subsection. (Ord. 09-2007, 8-13-2007)
8-10-3: NONCONFORMING BUILDINGS AND STRUCTURES:
   A.   Repairs, Maintenance And Alterations: Ordinary repairs, maintenance and
alterations may be made to a nonconforming building or structure; except, that
no structural alteration shall be made in or to such building or structure
except those required by law and except those making the building or structure
and use thereof conform, or more closely conform, to the regulations of the
district in which it is located.
   B.   Additions Or Enlargements: A building or structure which is
nonconforming as to bulk shall not be added to or enlarged in any manner unless
such building or structure and the use thereof, including all additions and
enlargements thereto, are made to conform to all the regulations of the
district in which it is located.
   C.   Moving To Another Location: A building or structure which does not
conform to all of the regulations of the district in which it is located shall
not be moved, in whole or in part, to any other location unless every portion
of such building or structure which is moved and the use thereof are made to
conform to all the regulations of the district into which it is moved.
   D.   Destruction Or Damage:
      1.   In all districts, a nonconforming residential building which is
destroyed or damaged by fire or other casualty or by an act of God may be
restored to its condition prior to the occurrence. (Ord., 10-11-1999)
      2.   In any district, a nonresidential nonconforming building or
structure which is destroyed or damaged by fire or other casualty or by an act
of God shall not be restored if the cost of restoration to its condition prior
to the occurrence exceeds fifty percent (50%) of the cost of restoring the
entire building or structure to like new condition unless said building or
structure and the use thereof shall conform thereafter to all the regulations
of the district in which it is located.
      3.   In the event that such damage or destruction is less than fifty
percent (50%) of the cost of restoration of an entire building or structure to
like new condition, the building or structure may be restored to its original
nonconforming condition only if such restoration is started within one hundred
twenty (120) days from the date of the partial damage or destruction and is
diligently prosecuted to completion. (Ord., 10-11-1999; amd. 2017 Code)
   E.   Abandonment Of Structures; Removal Of Mobile Homes: A nonconforming
building, structure or portion thereof which is unoccupied or unused for thirty
(30) days on and after the effective date hereof or thereafter becomes
unoccupied or unused and remains unoccupied or unused for any continuous thirty
(30) day period, or a lot upon which is situated a mobile home and the mobile
home is removed from said lot for a continuous thirty (30) day period, shall
not thereafter be occupied except by a use which conforms to the use
regulations of the district in which it is located. (Ord., 10-11-1999)
8-10-4: NONCONFORMING USES OF BUILDINGS AND STRUCTURES:
   A.   Expansion Of Use: A nonconforming use of a part of a building or
structure shall not be expanded or extended into any other portion of such
building or structure, nor changed to any other nonconforming use.
   B.   Discontinuance Of Use: If a nonconforming use of a building or
structure is discontinued for a period of six (6) months, it shall not be
renewed, and any subsequent use of the building or structure shall conform to
the use regulations of the district in which the building or structure is
located. Occupancy of such building or structure shall not be permitted prior
to inspection and issuance of a certificate of occupancy and use.
   C.   Change Of Use: A nonconforming use of a building or structure shall not
be changed to another nonconforming use. (Ord., 10-11-1999)
8-10-5: NONCONFORMING USE OF LAND:
   A.   Expansion Of Use: A nonconforming use of land shall not be expanded or
extended beyond the area it occupies on the effective date hereof.
   B.   Discontinuance Of Use: If a nonconforming use of land is discontinued
for a period of six (6) months, it shall not thereafter be renewed, and any
subsequent use of the land shall conform to the regulations of the district in
which the land is located.
   C.   Change Of Use: A nonconforming use of land shall not be changed to any
other use except to a use permitted in the district in which the land is
located. (Ord., 10-11-1999)
CHAPTER 3
ADMINISTRATION AND ENFORCEMENT
ARTICLE B.  SPECIAL USES
SECTION:
8-3B-1: Introduction
8-3B-2: Application For Special Use
8-3B-3: Hearing And Notice
8-3B-4: Zoning Board Findings Of Fact And Recommendations
8-3B-5: City Council Action
8-3B-1: INTRODUCTION:
The development and execution of this title is based upon the division of the
city into districts, within which districts the uses of land and buildings and
the yard and location of buildings and structures in relation to the land are
substantially uniform. It is recognized, however, that there are special uses
which, because of their unique characteristics, cannot be properly classified
in any particular district or districts without consideration, in each case, of
the impact of those uses upon neighboring land and of the public need for the
particular use at the particular location. Such special uses fall into the
following categories: (Ord., 10-11-1999; amd. 2017 Code)
   A.   Uses publicly operated or traditionally connected with a public
interest.
   B.   Uses entirely private in character, but of such an unusual nature that
their operation may give rise to unique problems with respect to their impact
upon neighboring property or public facilities. (Ord., 10-11-1999)
8-3B-2: APPLICATION FOR SPECIAL USE:
Any person who has a freehold interest in land, or a possessory interest
entitled to exclusive possession, or a contractual interest which may become a
freehold interest, or an exclusive possessory interest which is specifically
enforceable may file an application to use land for a special use provided in
this title in the zoning district in which the land is located. An application
for a special use permit, including a planned residential development special
use permit, shall be filed with and on a form available from the zoning
administrator. The application shall be accompanied by such plans and/or data
prescribed by the zoning board, and shall include a statement in writing by the
applicant and adequate evidence showing that the proposed special use will
conform to the standards set forth in the guidelines for applicants. The fee
for such an application shall be as set out in section 8-3-5 of this chapter.
(Ord., 10-11-1999; amd. 2017 Code)
8-3B-3: HEARING AND NOTICE:
Upon receipt in proper form of the application and statement referred to in
this article, the zoning board shall hold at least one public hearing on the
proposed special use. Not more than thirty (30) days nor less than fifteen (15)
days in advance of such hearing, notice of the time and place of such hearing
shall be published in a newspaper of general circulation in the city, as
prescribed by applicable state statutes. Supplemental or additional notices may
be published or distributed as the zoning board may, by rule, prescribe from
time to time. (Ord., 10-11-1999; amd. 2017 Code)
8-3B-4: ZONING BOARD FINDINGS OF FACT AND RECOMMENDATIONS:
   A.   Within thirty (30) days after the close of the public hearing on a
special use permit application, the zoning board shall make written findings of
fact and shall submit same, together with its recommendations, to the city
council. The city council shall make findings based upon the evidence presented
to it in each specific case that: (Ord., 10-11-1999; amd. 2017 Code)
      1.   The establishment, maintenance or operation of the special use will
not be detrimental to or endanger the public health, safety, comfort or general
welfare.
      2.   The special use will not be injurious to the use and enjoyment of
other property in the immediate vicinity for the purpose already permitted, nor
substantially diminished or property values impaired within the neighborhood.
      3.   The establishment of the special use will not impede the normal and
orderly development and improvement of the surrounding property for uses
permitted in the district.
      4.   Adequate utilities, access roads, drainage and/or necessary
facilities have been or are being provided, to include curbing, if deemed
necessary by the city council, sewer and water lines to the property line,
subject to approval by the engineer, architect or such other expert as the city
deems necessary.
      5.   Adequate measures have been or will be taken to provide ingress and
egress so designed as to minimize traffic congestion in the public streets.
(Ord., 10-11-1999)
      6.   The special use shall, in all other respects, conform to the
applicable regulations of the district in which it is located except as such
regulations may, in each instance, be modified by the city council pursuant to
the recommendations of the zoning board.
   B.   For each application for a special use permit, the zoning board shall
report to the city council the stipulations or additional conditions and
guarantees to be complied with by the applicant when they are deemed necessary
for the protection of the public interest. (Ord., 10-11-1999; amd. 2017 Code)
8-3B-5: CITY COUNCIL ACTION:
Any action taken by the city council with regard to special uses shall be by
ordinance. (Ord., 10-11-1999)
